Resolving Conflicts Between Equal Hadith Chains
Ruling on equal transmitter chains

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for resolving conflicting hadith chains when transmitters are equal in memory and precision, distinguishing between equal number and unequal number cases.

Core Idea
Equal transmitters: if numbers equal, suspend; if numbers unequal, prefer majority.

This passage presents a key methodological principle for weighing conflicting hadith reports. When the transmitters on both sides are equally reliable, the next step is to compare their numbers. The author lays down two clear scenarios: numerical parity requires suspension until a preponderating factor emerges, while numerical majority decides the case.

Guided Path
1
Identify Equality of Memory and Precision
First confirm that the transmitters on both sides are equal in terms of memory (hifz) and precision (itqan). If not, other rules apply.
Equality in reliability is the starting premise of this rule.
2
Check Numerical Equality
If the two sides have the same number of transmitters, then suspension (tawaqquf) is required until a preponderating factor (qarinah) appears that tilts the balance toward one side.
Preponderating factors are numerous and case-specific; there is no fixed list.
3
Apply Numerical Majority Rule
If one side has more transmitters than the other, judgment is given to the more numerous side. This holds even if some critics object.
The author states that the correct view is to follow the majority.
4
Recognize the Scope of Preponderance Factors
Understand that preponderance factors are broad and not limited to a fixed set. Each hadith may have its own unique factors that a skilled practitioner can discern by collecting many chains.
This emphasizes the role of expertise in hadith criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ تكلم - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - عن مَسالِك العُلَمَاء واختلافهم في كيفية التعامل مع هذه الأنواع فَقَالَ: «وإن المختلفين إما أن يكونوا متماثلين في الحفظ والإتقان أم لا. فالمتماثلون إما أن يكون عددهم من الجانبين سَوَاء أم لا، فإن استوى عددهم مع استواء أوصافهم وجب التوقف حَتَّى يترجح أحد الطريقين بقرينة من القرائن، فمتى اعتضدت إحدى الطريقين بشيء من وجوه الترجيح حكم لَهَا. ووجوه الترجيح كثيرة لا تنحصر ، ولا ضابط لَهَا بالنسبة إلى جَمِيع بَلْ كُلّ حَدِيث يقوم بِهِ ترجيح خاص لا يخفى على الممارس الفطن الذي أكثر من جمع الطرق ؛ ولأجل هَذَا كَانَ مجال النظر في هَذَا أكثر من غيره. وإن كان أحد المتماثلين أكثر عدداً فالحكم لَهُمْ عَلَى قَوْل الأكثر . ذَلِكَ. الأحاديث، وَقَدْ ذهب قوم إلى تعليله - وإن كَانَ من وصل أو رفع أكثر - وَالصَّحِيح خلاف ذَلِكَ.
Then he spoke – may Allah have mercy on him – about the methods of the scholars and their differences in how to deal with these types, and he said: 'The disagreeing parties are either equal in memory and precision or not. Those who are equal are either equal in number on both sides or not. If their number is equal and their qualities are equal, then suspension is necessary until one of the two paths is preponderated by some circumstantial evidence. When one path is supported by any aspect of preponderance, judgment is given in its favor. The aspects of preponderance are many and cannot be enumerated, and there is no specific rule for all. Rather, each hadith has a specific preponderance that is not hidden from the skilled practitioner who has collected many chains. For this reason, the scope of research in this area is greater than others. If one of the equal parties is greater in number, then judgment is for them according to the majority opinion. Some people go to criticizing it even if the one who connects or raises (the chain) is more, but the correct view is contrary to that.'
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage provides the methodology for dealing with conflicting hadith chains when the transmitters are equal in memory and precision. The author outlines two scenarios: (1) If the number of transmitters on both sides is equal and their qualities are equal, then one must suspend judgment until a preponderating factor (qarinah) emerges. These preponderating factors are many and depend on the specific hadith. (2) If one side has a larger number of transmitters, the majority view takes precedence, even if a minority criticizes the narration by claiming it is defective. The correct view, according to the author, is to favor the more numerous transmitters. This emphasizes the principle of numerical strength in hadith criticism when other factors are equal.

Key Terms
المتماثلين (al-mutamathilayn): Transmitters who are equal in memory and precision.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment until preponderance is established.
وجوه الترجيح (wujuh al-tarjih): Aspects or factors that give preponderance to one narration over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must be done when two groups of transmitters are equal in number and qualities?
A) Accept both equally
B) Suspend judgment until a preponderating factor appears
C) Prefer the group with higher memory
D) Prefer the group with older age

Key Takeaway
When transmitters are equal, numerical superiority decides; if numbers equal, seek a preponderating factor.

Chain Disagreement with Trustworthy Narrators: The Hanafi Position
Usul dispute: chain disagreement and its effect on hadith authenticity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that chain disagreement between trustworthy narrators does not harm the hadith, and distinguish this from cases involving weak narrators.

Core Idea
If both narrators are trustworthy, chain disagreement does not harm; proof stands from either side.

This passage addresses a key debate in hadith criticism: does a difference in the chain of transmission (sanad) undermine the reliability of a hadith when all narrators are trustworthy? The Hanafi school, aligning with the author, holds that it does not, because each trustworthy chain independently establishes proof. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the rebuttal of opposing views.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: when both narrators in conflicting chains are trustworthy, the disagreement does not harm the hadith's authenticity.
This is the position of the majority (al-akthar) according to the text.
2
Identify the opposing view
State the view of many hadith scholars: disagreement indicates lack of precision and harms the hadith unless dual hearing is proven.
This is the view the author criticizes as weak.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The key proof: each chain goes back to a trustworthy person, so the hadith is proven. The Sahihayn contain many such examples.
The Hanafi response relies on the principle that a trustworthy narrator's report is proof regardless of variant chains.
4
Evaluate the opposing proof
Opponents argue that difference shows lack of precision. The author rebuts that this is weak because the chain remains trustworthy; the possibility of dual hearing further strengthens it.
The author also notes a qualification: the hadith must be safe from being erroneous or anomalous (shadhdh).
5
Apply to weak narrator cases
When one narrator is weak, the weak chain is treated like a pause (waqf) or irsal, and normal preponderance rules apply. The possibility of dual hearing still exists if the narrator is prolific.
This shows the boundary of the rule: it applies only when all narrators are trustworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ قَالَ: «هذِهِ جملة تقسيم الاختلاف، وبقي إذا كَانَ رِجَال أحد الإسنادين أحفظ ورجال الآخر أكثر . فَقَد اختلف المتقدمون فيه: فمنهم من يرى قَوْل الأحفظ أولى لإتقانه وضبطه. ومنهم من يرى قَوْل الأكثر أولى لبعدهم عن الوهم. ثُمَّ قَالَ - بَعْدَ أن علل لما سبق -: «وأما النوع الرابع: وهُوَ الاختلاف في السَّنَد فلا يخلو إما أن يَكُون الرجلان ثقتين أم لا. فإن كانا ثقتين فلا يضر الاختلاف عِنْدَ الأكثر، لقيام الحجة بكل منهما، فكيفما دار الإسناد كَانَ عن ثقة، وربما احتمل أن يَكُون الرَّاوِي سمعه مِنْهُمَا جميعاً ، وَقَدْ وَجَدَ ذَلِكَ في كَثِير من الحَدِيْثِ، لَكِنْ ذَلِكَ يقوى حَيْثُ يَكُون الرَّاوِي مِمَّنْ لَهُ اعتناء بالطلب وتكثير الطرق»). ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وأما ما ذهب إليه كَثِير من أهل الحَدِيث من أن الاختلاف دليل عَلَى عدم ضبطه في الجملة فيضر ذَلِكَ وَلَوْ كَانَتْ رواته ثقات إلا أن يقوم دليل عَلَى أَنَّهُ عِنْدَ الرَّاوِي المختلف عَلَيْهِ عَنْهُمَا جميعاً أو بالطريقتين جميعاً؛ فَهُوَ رأي فِيهِ ضعف، لأَنَّهُ كيفما دار كَانَ عَلَى ثِقَة، وَفِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ من ذَلِكَ جملة أحاديث، لكن لا بد في الحكم بصحة ذَلِكَ سلامته من أن يَكُون غلطاً أو شاذاً. وأما إذا كَانَ أحد الراويين المختلف فيهما ضعيفاً لا يحتج به فههنا مجال للنظر، وتكون تِلْكَ الطَّرِيق الَّتِي سمي ذَلِكَ الضَّعِيف فِيْهَا، وجعل الحَدِيث عَنْهُ كالوقف أو الإرسال بالنسبة إلى الطريق الأخرى، فكل ما ذكر هناك من الترجيحات يجيء هنا. ويمكن أن يقال في مِثْل هَذَا يحتمل أن يَكُون الرَّاوِي إِذا كَانَ مكثراً قَدْ سمعه مِنْهُمَا - أيضاً - كَمَا تقدم. فإن قِيلَ : إذا كَانَ الحَدِيث عنده عن الثّقَة، فَلِمَ يرويه عن الضعيف؟ فالجواب: يحتمل أَنَّهُ لَمْ يطلع عَلَى ضعف شيخه أو اطلع(٢) عَلَيْهِ، ولكن ذكره اعتماداً عَلَى صِحَّة الحَدِيث عنده من الجهة الأخرى.
Then he said: 'This is a summary of the division of disagreement, and what remains is if the men of one chain are more precise and the men of the other are more numerous. The early scholars differed: some consider the view of the most precise better because of his accuracy and control, while others consider the view of the majority better because they are far from error.' Then he said – after providing reasoning for what preceded –: 'As for the fourth type, which is the disagreement in the chain, it is either that the two men are trustworthy or not. If they are both trustworthy, then the disagreement does not harm according to most, because proof is established through each of them. However the chain goes, it is from a trustworthy person, and it is possible that the narrator heard it from both of them. This is found in many hadiths, but this strengthens when the narrator is one who pays attention to seeking and collecting chains.' Then he said: 'As for what many hadith scholars have held, that disagreement indicates lack of precision in general and harms even if the narrators are trustworthy – unless evidence shows that the narrator in question heard from both or via both paths – this is a weak opinion, because however it goes, it is upon a trustworthy person, and in the two Sahihs there are many such hadiths. However, for the ruling of its correctness, it must be safe from being an error or anomalous. As for when one of the two differing narrators is weak and not acceptable, here there is scope for examination. That path that mentions the weak one is considered like a pause or irsal in relation to the other path, and all the preponderances mentioned there apply here. It can be said in such a case that if the narrator is prolific, he may have heard it from both – also – as mentioned earlier. If it is said: when the hadith is from a trustworthy source, why does he narrate it from the weak? The answer: it is possible that he was not aware of the weakness of his shaykh, or he was aware but mentioned it relying on the correctness of the hadith from the other side.'
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed exposition of the fourth type of disagreement in the chain (sanad). The author first notes a prior issue: when one chain's narrators are more precise but the other chain's narrators are more numerous, early scholars differed on which to prefer. Then he addresses the fourth type directly. He states that if both narrators in the two conflicting chains are trustworthy, the disagreement does not harm according to most scholars, because each chain independently establishes proof. The possibility that the narrator heard from both sides is real, especially if the narrator is a diligent collector. Ibn Hajar then refutes the view of many hadith scholars who say that difference indicates lack of precision and harms the hadith even if narrators are trustworthy, unless there is evidence of dual hearing. He argues that this view is weak because each chain goes back to a trustworthy person, and cites examples from the two Sahih collections. However, he adds a qualification: the hadith must be safe from error or anomaly. When one narrator is weak, the weak chain is treated like a disconnected or stopped narration, and the normal rules of preponderance apply. He also addresses a possible objection: why would a trustworthy narrator transmit from a weak source? The answer is that he may not know the weakness, or he may rely on the correctness from the other chain.

Key Terms
الاختلاف في السند (al-ikhtilaf fi al-sanad): Disagreement in the chain of transmission, e.g., variations in narrators.
الوقف (al-waqf): Stopping the hadith at a companion, not attributing to the Prophet.
الإرسال (al-irsal): Sending the hadith from a tabi'i directly to the Prophet without mentioning the companion.
ثقة (thiqah): Trustworthy narrator; reliable in transmission.
الشاذ (al-shadhdh): Anomalous hadith that contradicts a more reliable version.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the ruling when both narrators in a conflicting chain are trustworthy?
A) The difference harms and the hadith is rejected
B) The difference does not harm because each chain is from a trustworthy source
C) The hadith must be confirmed by a third chain
D) The narrator must have heard it from both

Key Takeaway
Chain disagreement between trustworthy narrators does not harm the hadith; each chain independently establishes proof.

Fifth and Sixth Types of Chain Disagreement
Explanation of two chain disagreement types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fifth and sixth types of chain disagreement and apply the rule that an ambiguous narrator in one chain is resolved by a named narrator in another, and that wording differences with identical meaning do not constitute contradiction.

Core Idea
An ambiguous narrator in one chain is the same named narrator in another; mere wording differences do not create contradiction.

This lesson explores two types of disagreements in hadith chains: the addition of a narrator (deferred) and variations in names and lineages. Understanding these rules helps us reconcile apparent contradictions between different transmissions and strengthens our confidence in the reliability of the hadith. The passage explains the first two divisions of the sixth type, providing clear criteria for when differences are harmful and when they are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of chain disagreement
Determine whether the disagreement is an added narrator (fifth type) or a variance in name/lineage (sixth type). The fifth type is deferred to a later discussion.
2
For name variance, classify the division
The sixth type has four divisions. This passage covers the first two: (1) narrator ambiguous in one chain, named in another; (2) only wording difference with same meaning.
3
Apply the reconciliation rule
For the first division: the ambiguous narrator is considered the same as the named one; if different, the named trustworthy narration outweighs. For the second division: wording differences are not considered contradictions if the meaning is identical and the narrator is trustworthy.
4
Understand the rationale
The rationale is that the ambiguity is resolved by the named version, and wording differences without meaning change are trivial, so they do not affect reliability.
5
Note the deferred treatment
The fifth type (added narrator) is not detailed here but will be explained later; its inclusion acknowledges that not all disagreements are covered immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النوع الخامس: وَهُوَ زيادة الرجل بَيْنَ الرجلين في السند فسيأتي تفصيله في النوع السابع والثلاثين – إن شاء الله - فَهُوَ في مكانه(۳). وأما النوع السادس: وَهُوَ الاختلاف في اسم الرَّاوِي ونسبه فَهُوَ عَلَى أقسام أربعة:
القسم الأول: أن يبهم في طريق وَيُسَمَّى في أخرى، فالظاهر أن هَذَا لا تعارض فيهِ؛ لأَنَّهُ يَكُون المُبْهَم في إحدى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ هُوَ المعين في الأخرى، وعلى تقدير أن يَكُون غيره، فَلا تضر رِوَايَة من سماه وعرفه إذا كَانَ ثِقَة - رواية من أبهمه. القِسْم الثَّانِي: أن يَكُون الاختلاف في العبارة فَقَط ، والمَعْنَى بِهَا في الكل واحد، فَإِنَّ مِثْل هَذَا لا يعد اختلافاً - أيضاً - ولا يضر إذا كَانَ الرَّاوِي ثِقَة.
As for the fifth type, which is the addition of a man between two men in the chain, its detail will come in the thirty-seventh type – God willing – so it is in its place. As for the sixth type, which is the disagreement in the name and lineage of the narrator, it is of four divisions: First division: That (the narrator) is ambiguous in one path and named in another. The apparent view is that there is no conflict here, because the ambiguous one in one narration is the specific one in the other. Assuming it is someone else, the narration of the one who named him and knew him does not harm if he is trustworthy – as opposed to the narration of the one who left him ambiguous. Second division: That the disagreement is only in expression, and the meaning in all is the same. Such is not considered disagreement – also – and does not harm if the narrator is trustworthy.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage covers the fifth and sixth types of disagreement in chains of transmission. The fifth type is the addition of a narrator between two known narrators in one chain. The author Ibn Hajar postpones its detailed treatment to the thirty-seventh type of his work, indicating it will be discussed later. The sixth type concerns disagreement in the name or lineage of a narrator, and it has four divisions. The text mentions the first two: (1) When a narrator is left anonymous (mubham) in one chain but named in another: the apparent ruling is that there is no conflict because the anonymous one is likely the same named person. Even if it were someone else, the narration from the person who named him (if trustworthy) outweighs the anonymous narration. (2) When the disagreement is only in expression (wording) but the meaning is the same — e.g., different ways of stating the same name — this is not considered a true contradiction and does not harm the hadith, especially if the narrator is trustworthy. The third and fourth divisions are not mentioned here, but the text indicates there are four in total.

Key Terms
المبهم (al-mubham): A narrator who is mentioned ambiguously without specifying his name.
الاختلاف في العبارة (al-ikhtilaf fi al-ibarah): Disagreement only in the wording or expression, while the meaning is identical.
زيادة الرجل بين الرجلين (ziyadat al-rajul bayna al-rajulayn): Addition of an extra narrator between two usually consecutive narrators in the chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a narrator is ambiguous in one chain but named in another?
A) It is a contradiction because the identities are unknown
B) There is no conflict; the ambiguous one is likely the same as the named one
C) The ambiguous chain is preferred
D) Both chains are rejected

Key Takeaway
Not all differences in chain narrators are contradictions; many are resolvable by considering the same identity or equivalent meaning.

Conditions for Ittisal in Hadith Chains
Defining ittisal and its conditions within the context of idtirab in sanad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for ittisal in a hadith chain and apply them to determine whether a narration meets the Hanafi requirement for accepting a hadith as proof.

Core Idea
Connection is not assumed from ambiguous phrases; it requires freedom from tadlis and contemporaneity with possibility of meeting.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the authenticity of a hadith depends heavily on the connection (ittisal) of its chain. This lesson unpacks the definition of ittisal, the explicit and ambiguous formulas narrators use, and the conditions under which ambiguous formulas can be accepted. Understanding these conditions is essential for evaluating whether a hadith can serve as evidence in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Define ittisal and its role
Ittisal means that each narrator heard the hadith directly from his immediate teacher. It is a fundamental condition for a sahih hadith.
The passage emphasizes ittisal as the first condition in defining sahih.
2
Distinguish explicit from ambiguous formulas
Explicit formulas like haddathana, akhbarana, sami'tu clearly indicate audition. Ambiguous formulas like 'an, anna, or qala require further verification.
Even explicit formulas can be mistaken, as noted by Ibn Rajab.
3
Identify the two core conditions for ambiguous formulas
For ambiguous phrases, two conditions must be met: (1) the narrator is not a mudallis, and (2) there is contemporaneity and possibility of meeting between narrator and teacher.
Some scholars add a third condition: proven actual meeting.
4
Apply the conditions to a sample chain
Given a chain with a narrator using 'an', check if he is known for tadlis and if they were contemporaries. If both conditions hold, assume ittisal; otherwise, the chain is considered disconnected.
This judgment affects whether a hadith is accepted as dalil in fiqh.

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
قُلْتُ القائل ابن حجر وبهذا يتبين أن تمثيل المصنف (١) للمضطرب بحديث أبي عمرو بن حريث لَيْسَ بمستقيم انتهى. القسم الثالث: أن يقع التصريح باسم الرَّاوِي ونسبه لكن مع الاختلاف في سياق ذلِكَ» (٢). ثُمَّ ساق مثالاً لِذلِكَ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «القِسْم الرابع: أن يقع التصريح به من غير اختلاف لَكِنْ يَكُون ذَلِكَ من متفقين: أحدهما ثِقَة، والآخر ضَعِيف. أو أحدهما مستلزم الاتصال، والآخر الإرسال كما قدمناه (٣).
ولما كَانَ الاضطراب يقع في السَّنَد والمثن رأيت أن أفضل الاضطراب الواقع السَّنَد؛ لأَنَّهُ الأهم والأكثر تشعباً مَعَ بيان أمثلته، ثُمَّ أسوق أثر ذَلِكَ في الفُقَهَاء ثُمَّ الكلام عن اضطراب المثن. وَقَدْ جعلت كلاً مِنْهُمَا فِي نَوع مستقل:
في القسم الأول الاضطراب في السند
بالنظر لما تمتع به الإسناد من أهمية في حياة الأمة الإسلامية كونه من أهم خصائصها، فَقَدْ حضي بالاهتمام من حَيْثُ الحفاظ عَلَيْهِ والتنقير والتفتيش عن صحيحه وضَعِيفه، وَقَدِ اهتم السلف الصالح بحفظ مئات الألوف من الأسانيد، وبينوا قويها من سقيمها حَتَّى خرجوا لَنَا ببحوث ونتائج قل نظيرها. والسند كَمَا يَكُون مِنْهُ الصَّحِيح والأصح ، ففيه الضَّعِيف والمعلول، والذي تدخله العلة من الأسانيد كَثِير لَيْسَ بقليل، وَقَدْ رأيت أن أحسن من صنفها الحافظ العلائي). وسأفصل الكلام عن كُلّ نَوْع بكلام مستقل
النوع الأول : تعارض الوصل والإرسال
الوصل هنا بمعنى الاتصال، والاتصال هُوَ أحد الشروط الأساسية في صحة الحَدِيث بَلْ هُوَ ،أولها، قال العراقي في نظمه:
إلى صَحِيْحٍ وَضَعِيْفَ وَحَسَنْ وَأَهْلُ هَذَا الشَّأْنِ قَسَّمُوا السُّنَنْ
بِنَقْلِ عَدْلِ ضَابِط الْفُؤَادِ فَالأَوَّلُ الْمُتَصلُ الإِسْنَادِ وَعِلَّةٍ قَادِحَةٍ فَتُوْذِي ) عَنْ مِثْلِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ مَا شُدُوْنِ وكل من عرّف الصَّحِيح أبتدأ أولاً بذكر الاتصال (٢)، والاتصال: هُوَ سَمَاع الحَدِيث لكل راو من الرَّاوِي الَّذِي يليه(٣).
ويعرف الاتصال بتصريح الرَّاوِي بإحدى صيغ السَّماع الصريحة، وَهِيَ حَدَّثَنَا، وَقَالَ لَنَا، وسمعت، وأخبرنا، وأنبأنا، وغيرها من الصيغ. وهذا هُوَ الأصل. وربما حصل التصريح في السَّماع في بَعْض الأسانيد، لَكِنْ صيارفة الحَدِيث ونقاده يحكمون بخطأ هذا التصريح، ثُمَّ الحكم عَلَى الرِّوَايَة بالانقطاع ، قَالَ ابن رجب وَكَانَ أحمد (٤) يستنكر دخول التحديث في كثير من الأسانيد، ويقول: هُوَ خطأ، يعني ذكر السَّمَاع». وَقَدْ بحث ابن رجب ذَلِكَ بحثاً واسعاً، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وحينئذٍ ينبغي التفطن لهذه الأمور، ولا يغتر بمجرد ذكر السَّماع والتحديث في الأسانيد، فَقَدْ ذكر ابن المديني: أن شُعْبَة وجدوا له غَيْر شيء يذكر فيهِ الإخبار عن شيوخه، ويكون منقطعاً).
وأعود إلى التفصيل السابق ثُمَّ أقول: أما إذا كَانَتِ الرّوَايَة بصيغة من الصيغ المحتملة، مثل: عن أو أن أو حدث، أو أخبر أو قَالَ، فحينئذ يَجِبُ توفر شرطين في الرَّاوِي لحمل هذِهِ الصيغة عَلَى الاتصال:
الشرط الأول السلامة من التَّدْلِيس أي أن لا يَكون من رَوَى هكذا مدلساً.
الشرط الثاني المعاصرة وإمكان اللقاء، وَقَدِ اكتفى بهذين الشرطين كثير من المُحَدِّثِينَ، وأضاف عَلَي بن المديني والبُخَارِيّ وآخرون شرطاً ثالثاً، وَهُوَ: ثبوت اللقاء
Chapter Three / Difference in Sanad and Matn. I said - the speaker is Ibn Hajar - and by this it becomes clear that the author's (1) example of mudtarib with the hadith of Abu 'Amr ibn Huraith is not correct. End. The third division: that the name and lineage of the narrator are explicitly mentioned but with difference in the context of that (2). Then he gave an example for that, then he said: 'The fourth division: that explicit mention occurs without difference, but it is from two [narrators] who agree: one is trustworthy and the other weak. Or one necessitates connection and the other disconnection as we have presented (3).' And since idtirab occurs in sanad and matn, I saw that I should prioritize idtirab occurring in the sanad because it is more important and more branched out, along with showing its examples. Then I will present the effect of that on the jurists, then discussion about idtirab in matn. And I have made each of them in an independent type: In the first section: Idtirab in Sanad. Considering the importance that isnad enjoys in the life of the Islamic nation, being one of its most important characteristics, it has received attention in terms of preserving it and scrutinizing and searching its authentic and weak. The righteous predecessors took care to preserve hundreds of thousands of asanid, and distinguished its strong from its weak until they produced for us research and results rarely matched. And just as from the sanad come the authentic and more authentic, it also contains the weak and defective, and that which is affected by a defect in asanid is many, not few. And I saw that the best of those who classified them is al-Hafiz al-'Ala'i (4). And I will detail the discussion on each type with independent speech. The first type: conflict between wasl and irsal. Wasl here means ittisal (connection), and ittisal is one of the basic conditions for the authenticity of hadith, rather it is the first of them. Al-'Iraqi said in his poem: 'The people of this field divided the sunan into authentic, weak, and good. The first is the connected chain of transmission, without any detrimental defect, transmitted by a trustworthy, precise person.' And everyone who defined authentic [hadith] began first by mentioning connection (2). And ittisal is: that each narrator hears the hadith from the narrator who precedes him (3). And connection is known by the narrator's explicit declaration using one of the explicit forms of audition, which are: haddathana, qala lana, sami'tu, akhbarana, anba'ana, and other forms. And this is the principle. And perhaps explicit mention of audition occurs in some asanid, but the money-changers and critics of hadith judge this explicit mention to be mistaken, then judge the narration to be disconnected. Ibn Rajab said: 'Ahmad (4) used to reject the inclusion of tahdith in many asanid and say: it is a mistake, meaning mentioning audition.' And Ibn Rajab researched that extensively, then said: 'Therefore it is necessary to pay attention to these matters, and not be deceived by mere mention of audition and tahdith in asanid. Ibn al-Madini mentioned that for Shu'ba they found something in which he reported from his teachers and it was disconnected.' And I return to the previous detail then I say: As for when the narration is with a probable form, such as 'an, anna, haddatha, akhbara, or qala, then two conditions must be met in the narrator to carry this form upon connection: The first condition: safety from tadlis, i.e., that he is not one who narrates thus while being a mudallis. The second condition: contemporaneity and possibility of meeting. Many muhaddithun sufficed with these two conditions. And 'Ali ibn al-Madini, al-Bukhari, and others added a third condition: verification of meeting.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the discussion on types of idtirab (disruption) in sanad and matn, and it moves to define the first type under idtirab in sanad: conflict between wasl and irsal (connection and disconnection). The author begins by quoting Ibn Hajar's criticism of Ibn al-Salah's example of mudtarib and then lists the third and fourth divisions of idtirab according to Ibn Hajar's classification in al-Nukat. The third division involves explicit mention of the narrator's name and lineage but with difference in the context; the fourth involves explicit mention without difference but from two narrators, one trustworthy and one weak, or one implying connection and the other disconnection. The author then explains his plan to first discuss idtirab in sanad due to its greater importance and complexity, followed by its effect on jurists, then idtirab in matn. He praises al-Hafiz al-'Ala'i's work on the subject. Under the first type, 'conflict between wasl and irsal', he defines ittisal (connection) as a fundamental condition for a hadith's authenticity, quoting al-'Iraqi's poetic definition. He explains that ittisal is established when each narrator explicitly states hearing from his immediate teacher using clear audition phrases like 'haddathana' or 'sami'tu'. However, he warns that sometimes explicit mentions are erroneous, citing Ibn Rajab's caution about relying on mere claims of audition. He then discusses cases where ambiguous phrases like 'an' are used, requiring two conditions: the narrator must not be a mudallis (one who tadlis), and there must be contemporaneity and possibility of meeting. Some scholars add a third condition: proven actual meeting. This discussion is foundational for evaluating the authenticity of ahadith and understanding how differences in sanad transmission affect fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
الاضطراب (al-idtirab): Disruption in the chain (sanad) or text (matn) of a hadith, often due to contradictory transmissions with no preferred version.
الاتصال (al-ittisal): The connection of the chain such that each narrator heard the hadith from his immediate teacher.
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing a defect in the chain by using ambiguous phrases or omitting a weak link.
المعاصرة وإمكان اللقاء (al-mu'asarah wa imkan al-liqa'): Contemporaneity and possibility of meeting between narrator and his reported teacher, allowing for the assumption of connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the minimum conditions to assume connection (ittisal) when a narrator uses an ambiguous phrase like 'an'?
A) The narrator must be trustworthy and the chain must be short.
B) The narrator must be free from tadlis and there must be contemporaneity with possibility of meeting.
C) The narrator must have explicitly stated hearing the hadith.
D) The hadith must be found in a reliable collection like Sahih al-Bukhari.

Key Takeaway
Ittisal requires either explicit audition or, for ambiguous phrases, safety from tadlis and contemporaneity with possibility of meeting.

Defining Ittisal and Its Conditions in Hanafi Usul
Defining connectedness and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ittisal, distinguish explicit from ambiguous hearing forms, and apply the conditions (no tadlis + contemporaneity) to determine whether a chain is connected.

Core Idea
Connectedness is established by explicit hearing terms; for ambiguous forms, two conditions must hold.

This passage from a Hanafi usul work clarifies the concept of ittisal (connectedness) in hadith chains, a foundational requirement for authoritative Sunnah. Understanding when a chain is truly connected—and when apparent connections may be invalid—is essential for proper legal derivation. The text defines ittisal, lists explicit hearing formulas, and sets conditions for ambiguous ones, while also warning that even explicit terms can be erroneous.

Guided Path
1
Define ittisal
Start with the definition: ittisal means that each narrator in the chain heard the hadith directly from his immediate teacher.
The text says: 'سماع الحديث لكل راو من الراوي الذي يليه'.
2
Identify explicit and ambiguous forms
Explicit forms (حَدَّثَنَا, أَخْبَرَنَا, سَمِعْتُ, etc.) indicate hearing clearly. Ambiguous forms ('عَنْ, أَنَّ, قَالَ) do not explicitly state hearing and require conditions to be considered connected.
3
Recognize that explicit forms are not infallible
Even if a narrator uses an explicit word, experts may rule it an error and declare the chain disconnected. The passage cites Ibn Rajab and Shu'bah as examples.
This shows that textual wording alone is insufficient; expert critique overrides.
4
State the two conditions for ambiguous forms
For forms like 'an, the narrator must (1) be free from tadlis (concealing flaws) and (2) be contemporaneous with the teacher, with possibility of meeting. Many muhaddithun accept these two; some add a third: actual proven meeting.
Hanafi usul generally follows the two-condition view, accepting 'an'anah from non-mudallisin with mu'asarah.

الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
بِنَقْلِ عَدْلِ ضَابِط الْفُؤَادِ فَالأَوَّلُ الْمُتَصلُ الإِسْنَادِ وَعِلَّةٍ قَادِحَةٍ فَتُوْذِي ) عَنْ مِثْلِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ مَا شُدُوْنِ وكل من عرّف الصَّحِيح أبتدأ أولاً بذكر الاتصال (۲)، والاتصال: هُوَ سَمَاع الحَدِيث لكل راو من الرَّاوِي الَّذِي يليه(۳).
ويعرف الاتصال بتصريح الرَّاوِي بإحدى صيغ السَّماع الصريحة، وَهِيَ حَدَّثَنَا، وَقَالَ لَنَا، وسمعت، وأخبرنا، وأنبأنا، وغيرها من الصيغ.
وهذا هُوَ الأصل. وربما حصل التصريح في السَّماع في بَعْض الأسانيد، لَكِنْ صيارفة الحَدِيث ونقاده يحكمون بخطأ هذا التصريح، ثُمَّ الحكم عَلَى الرِّوَايَة بالانقطاع ، قَالَ ابن رجب وَكَانَ أحمد (٤) يستنكر دخول التحديث في كثير من الأسانيد، ويقول: هُوَ خطأ، يعني ذكر السَّمَاع». وَقَدْ بحث ابن رجب ذَلِكَ بحثاً واسعاً، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وحينئذٍ ينبغي التفطن لهذه الأمور، ولا يغتر بمجرد ذكر السَّماع والتحديث في الأسانيد، فَقَدْ ذكر ابن المديني: أن شُعْبَة وجدوا له غَيْر شيء يذكر فيهِ الإخبار عن شيوخه، ويكون منقطعاً).
وأعود إلى التفصيل السابق ثُمَّ أقول: أما إذا كَانَتِ الرّوَايَة بصيغة من الصيغ المحتملة، مثل: عن أو أن أو حدث، أو أخبر أو قَالَ، فحينئذ يَجِبُ توفر شرطين في الرَّاوِي لحمل هذِهِ الصيغة عَلَى الاتصال:
الشرط الأول السلامة من التَّدْلِيس أي أن لا يَكون من رَوَى هكذا مدلساً.
الشرط الثاني المعاصرة وإمكان اللقاء، وَقَدِ اكتفى بهذين الشرطين كثير من المُحَدِّثِينَ، وأضاف عَلَي بن المديني والبُخَارِيّ وآخرون شرطاً ثالثاً، وَهُوَ: ثبوت اللقاء وَلَوْ مرة وَاحِدَة).
Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. 233. With the transmission of a just, precise, and reliable person, the first is the connected chain, and a harmful defect... (verses 11-13). Everyone who defined the sahih first mentions connectedness (2). And connectedness: it is the hearing of the hadith by each narrator from the narrator after him (3). And connectedness is known by the narrator explicitly stating one of the explicit forms of hearing, which are: haddathana, qala lana, sami'tu, akhbarana, anba'ana, and other forms. This is the original principle. Sometimes an explicit hearing statement occurs in some chains, but the experts and critics of hadith rule that this explicit statement is erroneous, then they rule the narration as disconnected. Ibn Rajab said: Ahmad (4) used to deny the occurrence of 'haddathana' in many chains and said: 'It is an error,' meaning the mention of hearing. And Ibn Rajab discussed this extensively, then said: 'Then one should be attentive to these matters and not be deceived by mere mention of hearing and 'haddathana' in chains, for Ibn al-Madini said: that they found for Shu'bah many things in which he reports from his shaykhs but it is disconnected.' I return to the previous detail and say: As for when the narration is in a probable form, such as 'an, anna, haddatha, akhbara, or qala, then two conditions must be present in the narrator to consider this form as connected: The first condition is freedom from tadlis, i.e., he should not be one who narrates in this way while being a mudallis. The second condition is contemporaneity and possibility of meeting, and many muhaddithun have sufficed with these two conditions, and Ali ibn al-Madini, al-Bukhari, and others added a third condition: establishment of meeting, even once.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of ittisal (connectedness) in hadith chains. The author begins by quoting a verse from al-'Iraqi's Alfiyyah. Then states that connectedness means each narrator heard the hadith from his immediate teacher. It is identified by explicit hearing words like haddathana, akhbarana, etc. However, if an explicit word appears but experts deem it a mistake, the chain is ruled disconnected. This shows that explicit wording is not always taken at face value. For ambiguous forms (like 'an), two conditions are required: the narrator must not be a mudallis, and they must be contemporaneous with possibility of meeting. A third condition, actual proof of meeting, is added by Ibn al-Madini and al-Bukhari. The passage clarifies that the default assumption of connection depends on these conditions.

Key Terms
الاتصال (al-ittisal): سماع الحديث لكل راو من الراوي الذي يليه (hearing of the hadith by each narrator from the one before him)
التَّدْلِيس (al-tadlis): أن يروي الراوي ما لم يسمعه بصيغة توهم السماع (narrating what one did not hear in a form implying hearing)
المعاصرة (al-mu'asarah): كون الراوي في عصر من روى عنه (being in the same era as one's teacher)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required to consider a narration using 'an' as connected, according to the majority of muhaddithun?
A) Actual meeting between narrator and teacher
B) Freedom from tadlis and contemporaneity with possibility of meeting
C) The narration must be found in Sahih al-Bukhari
D) The chain must be from a tabi'i

Key Takeaway
Connectedness of a hadith chain is established by explicit hearing terms, but experts may reject even explicit claims; for ambiguous forms, freedom from tadlis and contemporaneity are the accepted conditions.

Inqita' and Mursal: Definitions and Historical Usage
Explaining discontinuity in chains and the term mursal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the general concept of inqita' (discontinuity) and the specific term mursal as used by later scholars, and state the implications for hadith authenticity in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A chain broken anywhere is munqati'; only a break at the end (tabi'i skipping Companion) is mursal in later terminology.

Connectedness of the chain (ittiṣāl al-sanad) is a fundamental condition for a hadith to be considered authentic (ṣaḥīḥ). Any break in the chain weakens the narration. However, not all breaks are treated equally. This lesson clarifies the general term for discontinuity (inqita') and the specific term mursal, which underwent a historical narrowing of meaning. Understanding this evolution is crucial for correctly applying hadith criticism in Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Recognize that connectedness must apply from the beginning to the end of the chain; a break at any point violates this condition.
The condition is not limited to one layer.
2
Define inqita'
Any break in the chain at any position (beginning, middle, or end) is called inqita' and the hadith is munqati'.
In early usage, this was also called mursal.
3
Trace historical evolution
Note that earlier scholars used mursal for any break, but later terminology restricted it to breaks at the end where a tabi'i omits the Companion.
This specialization helps avoid confusion.
4
Focus on discontinuity at the end
The specific type of inqita' at the end of the chain is what later scholars call mursal: a tabi'i directly attributing to the Prophet.
This is the most relevant for usul al-fiqh discussions.
5
Relate to authenticity
Since connectedness is a condition for ṣaḥīḥ, any discontinuity (including mursal) indicates weakness, though Hanafi usul may accept mursal under certain conditions.
Weakness does not automatically mean rejection; context matters.

والاتصال في السَّنَد لا يشترط أن يَكُون في طبقة وَاحِدَة فَقَطْ بَلْ يشترط أن يَكُون من أول السَّنَد إلى آخره؛ فإذا اختل الاتصال في مَوْضِع من المواضع سمي منقطعاً، وَكَانَ يطلق عَلَيْهِ في القرون المتقدمة مرسلا (۳) ، ثُمَّ استقر الاصطلاح بعد عَلَى أن المُرْسَل هُوَ: ما أضافه التابعي إلى النبي . ولما كَانَ الاتصال شرطاً للصحة فالانقطاع ينافي الصحة، إذن الانقطاع أمارة من أمارات الضعف؛ لأن الضَّعِيف مَا فَقَدْ شرطاً من شروط الصحة (٤). والانقطاع قَدْ يَكُون في أول السَّنَد، وَقَدْ يَكُون في آخره، وَقَدْ يَكُون في وسطه، وَقَدْ يَكُون الانقطاع براو واحد أو أكثر. وكل ذَلِكَ من نَوْع الانقطاع، والذي يعنينا الكلام عَلَيْهِ هنا هُوَ الكلام عن الانقطاع في آخر الإسناد، وَهُوَ مَا يُسَمَّى بالمرسل عِنْدَ المتأخرين، وَهُوَ مَا أضافه التابعي إلى النبي ).
And connectedness in the chain does not have to be in only one layer, but rather it must be from the beginning of the chain to its end. So if connection is broken in any place, it is called disconnected, and in earlier centuries it was also called mursal (3). Then later terminology settled that mursal is: what a tabi'i attributes to the Prophet. Since connectedness is a condition for authenticity, discontinuity contradicts authenticity, so discontinuity is an indication of weakness, because the weak is what lacks a condition of authenticity (4). Discontinuity can be at the beginning of the chain, at its end, or in its middle, and it can be by one narrator or more. All of that is a type of discontinuity. What concerns us here is the discontinuity at the end of the chain, which is called mursal among later scholars, and it is what a tabi'i attributes to the Prophet.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage defines inqita' (discontinuity) and mursal as a specific subtype. It emphasizes that connectedness must apply to the entire chain from start to finish; any break invalidates it, and the entire chain is called disconnected (munqati'). The author notes that in early usage, any such break was called mursal, but later terminology restricted mursal to when a tabi'i directly ascribes to the Prophet, dropping the Companion. Since connectedness is a condition for sahih, discontinuity makes the hadith weak. Discontinuity can occur at any point, but the focus here is on breaks at the end, i.e., mursal. This is crucial for fiqh because mursal hadith is generally not accepted as proof in Hanafi usul, though with conditions it may be considered.

Key Terms
الانقطاع (al-inqita'): اختلال الاتصال في الإسناد في موضع من المواضع (break in the continuity of the chain at any point)
المرسل (al-mursal): ما أضافه التابعي إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (what a tabi'i attributes directly to the Prophet)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of mursal among later scholars?
A) Any chain with a missing narrator
B) A chain where a tabi'i narrates directly from the Prophet
C) A chain attributed to the Prophet with a Companion mentioned
D) A chain with discontinuity in the middle

Key Takeaway
Discontinuity at any point weakens a hadith, and the term mursal is specifically reserved for a break at the end where a tabi'i omits the Companion.

Tarjih of Hadith Chains: Sujud al-Sahw Before or After Salām?
Analyzing hadith chain and fiqh effect of sujud al-sahw position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply tarjih principles to conflicting hadith chains and identify the fiqh consequence for the ruling on sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
Quality and memory of narrators outweigh mere quantity in tarjih—here determining whether sujud al-sahw is before or after salām.

This passage demonstrates a key usul al-fiqh skill: weighing conflicting narrations of the same hadith. By examining the differences between mursal and muttasil versions of the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, you will see how the preference for the connected chain leads the majority of jurists to rule that sujud al-sahw is performed before the salam. You will also learn the principle that a stronger chain (even if fewer narrators) can override a more numerous but weaker one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting chains
Recognize that the hadith of Abu Sa'id was transmitted both as mursal (by several narrators) and muttasil (by fewer but more reliable narrators). Note the specific narrators and their chains given in the source.
The mursal version goes through Malik, Zayd, 'Ata; the muttasil version includes additional narrators linking to Abu Sa'id.
2
Apply tarjih principles
Understand the criteria used: number of narrators vs. their reliability (hifz). The text argues that muttasil is preponderant because its narrators are huffaz and are supported by multiple follow-ups.
The author contrasts the widespread mursal against the muttasil supported by Ibn 'Ajlan, 'Abd al-'Aziz, etc.
3
Evaluate the preference
See that even though mursal narrators are more numerous, the muttasil version is preferred due to quality and external confirmation from Ibn 'Abd al-Barr, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and al-Daraqutni.
Ibn 'Abd al-Barr: 'Those who connected it are memorizers whose addition is acceptable.'
4
Connect to fiqh ruling
Observe how accepting the muttasil version leads to the ruling that all sujud al-sahw are before salam, as held by the majority (including al-Shafi'i and Ahmad).
The hadith of Ibn Buhayna is also cited as supporting evidence.

الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
فَهؤلاء ثمانيتهم رووه عن مالك، عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء بن يسار، به.
والحديث رواه الوليد بن مُسْلِم، ويَحْيَى بن راشد المازني عن مالك، عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء بن يسار، عن أبي سعيد بهِ - متصلاً -. هكذا اختلف عَلَى الإمام مالك بن أنس في وصل هَذَا الحَدِيث وإرساله والراجح فِيهِ الوَصْل، وإن كَانَ رواة الإرسال أكثر وَهُوَ الصَّحِيح من رِوَايَة مَالِك، لما يأتي: وَهُوَ أن الإمام مالكاً توبع عَلَى وصل هَذَا الحَدِيث: فَقَدْ رَواهُ فليح بن سليمان، وعبد العزيز بن عبد الله بن أبي سلمة، وسليمان بن بلال، ومُحَمَّد بن مطرف، ومُحَمَّد بن عجلان رووه عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء بن يسار، عن أبي سعيد الخُدْرِيِّ، بِهِ متصلاً. وَقَدْ خالفهم جميعاً يعقوب بن عَبْد الرَّحْمن القاري فرواه عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء، مرسلاً. لَكِنْ روايته لَمْ تقاوم أمام رِوَايَة الجَمْع. إذن فالراجح في رِوَايَة هَذَا الحَدِيث الوَصْل لكثرة العدد وشدة الحفظ. قَالَ الحافظ ابن عَبْد البر : و الحَدِيث مُتَّصِل مُسْنَد صَحِيح، لا يضره تقصير من قصر به في اتصاله؛ لأن الَّذِيْنَ وصلوه حُفَّاظ مقبولة زيادتهم. وَقَالَ في مَوْضِع آخر : قَالَ الأثرم: سألت أحمد بن حنبل عن حَدِيث أبي سعيد في السهو، أتذهب إليه؟ قَالَ : نعم أذهب إليه، قلتُ: إنهم يختلفون في إسناده، قَالَ: إِنَّمَا قصر بِهِ مَالِك وَقَدْ أسنده عدة مِنْهُمْ : ابن عجلان وعبد العزيز بن أبي سلمة. ثُمَّ إِن هَذَا الحَدِيث قَد تناوله الإمام العراقي الجهبذ أبُو الحَسَن الدَّارَقُطْنِي في علله وانتهى إلى ترجيح الرواية المسندة.
أثر هَذَا الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء (موضع سجود السهو)
اختلف الفُقَهَاء في مَوْضِع سجود السهو؛ فذهب أكثر العُلَماء إلى تصحيح الرِّوَايَة الموصولة، وأخذوا بالحَدِيث السابق، وقالوا إن السجود كله قَبْلَ السلام، وَهُوَ قول أكثر الفُقَهَاء، وإليه ذهب الشافعي، وأحمد في رِوَايَة. وحَدِيث أبي سعيد نَص صريح عَلَى أن السجود في الزيادة قَبْلَ السلام. واحتجوا لذلك أيضاً بما رواه عبدالله بن بحينة؛ قَالَ: «صلى لَنَا رَسُوْلَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَكْعَتَيْنِ مِن بَعْضٍ الصلوات. ثُمَّ قام فَلَمْ يجلس. فقام الناس مَعَهُ فَلَمَّا قضى صلاته، ونظرنا تسليمه كبر
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text. These eight narrated it from Malik, from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from him. And the hadith was narrated by al-Walid ibn Muslim and Yahya ibn Rashid al-Mazini from Malik, from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from Abu Sa'id - connected. Thus there is disagreement over Imam Malik ibn Anas regarding connecting this hadith or sending it (mursal), and the preponderant view is the connection, even if the narrators of the mursal are more numerous, and it is the correct version from Malik's narration, because: Imam Malik was followed in connecting this hadith. Fulaij ibn Sulayman, 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Abdullah ibn Abi Salama, Sulayman ibn Bilal, Muhammad ibn Mutarrif, and Muhammad ibn 'Ajlan all narrated it from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, connected. And all of them were contradicted by Ya'qub ibn 'Abd al-Rahman al-Qari who narrated it from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata', as mursal. But his narration does not stand against the collective narration. So the preponderant version of this hadith is the connected one due to the abundance of narrators and strong memory. Al-Hafiz Ibn 'Abd al-Barr said: 'The hadith is connected, supported, authentic; the defect of those who shortened it in its connection does not harm it, because those who connected it are memorizers whose addition is acceptable.' And he said elsewhere: Al-Athram said: I asked Ahmad ibn Hanbal about the hadith of Abu Sa'id concerning forgetfulness, 'Do you adopt it?' He said: 'Yes, I adopt it.' I said: 'They differ in its chain.' He said: 'Only Malik shortened it, and several others narrated it connected among them: Ibn 'Ajlan and 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Abi Salama.' Then this hadith was examined by the expert Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni in his 'Ilal, and he concluded by preferring the connected narration. The effect of this hadith on the disagreement of jurists (Position of prostration of forgetfulness). The jurists differed regarding the position of the prostration of forgetfulness; the majority of scholars validated the connected narration, acted upon the aforementioned hadith, and said that all prostrations are before the salam. That is the view of the majority of jurists, and it was the view of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration. The hadith of Abu Sa'id is an explicit text that the prostration for increase is before the salam. They also used as evidence what 'Abdullah ibn Buhayna narrated: He said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prayed two rak'ahs of one of the prayers for us. Then he stood up and did not sit. So the people stood with him. When he finished his prayer and we looked for his taslim, he said the takbir...'
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a detailed case study in how differences in hadith chain (sanad) transmission lead to differences in fiqh rulings. The author first presents the dispute regarding the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness). Some narrators transmitted it as mursal (broken chain, not mentioning the Companion), while others transmitted it as muttasil (connected chain, with Abu Sa'id). The text argues that even though the mursal narrators are more numerous, the muttasil version is preponderant because the narrators who connected it are of higher quality (huffaz, strong memorizers) and they are supported by multiple follow-up narrations. The author cites Ibn 'Abd al-Barr and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal to reinforce this preference. Then, the passage shows the fiqh consequence: the majority of scholars (including al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration) accept the muttasil version and therefore rule that all prostrations of forgetfulness are performed before the salam. They also cite the hadith of Ibn Buhayna as supporting evidence. The passage does not explicitly mention the Hanafi position here, but the analysis demonstrates the usul principle that when chains conflict, preference is given based on the number and reliability of narrators (tarjih bi al-kathrah wa al-hifz). The text also shows the direct impact of isnad criticism on substantive law.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or error during prayer.
مُرسَل (mursal): A hadith where the chain is broken by omitting the Companion, i.e., a Successor narrates directly from the Prophet.
مُتَّصِل (muttasil): A hadith with a continuous chain of transmission all the way back to the Prophet.
تَرجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one version or opinion over another based on strength of evidence.

C) Both versions are equally valid
D) The version transmitted by Ya'qub al-Qari

Key Takeaway
Chain analysis (tarjih al-asaneed) directly impacts fiqh rulings: the preference for the muttasil version of Abu Sa'id's hadith led the majority to rule that sujud al-sahw is before salam.

How Hadith Chain Disagreement Shapes Sajda al-Sahw Ruling
Analyzing chain differences in hadith and their effect on fiqh ruling of sajda al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze how a disagreement in the hadith chain (mursal vs. mawsool) leads to a difference in the fiqh ruling of sajda al-sahw between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
A hadith's chain strength determines its legal weight, but jurists may still differ based on preferred proofs.

The position of sajda al-sahw in prayer is a classic example of how a seemingly minor chain disagreement can produce a major fiqh difference. This lesson examines the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, its chain variants, and how the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) and the majority (including al-Shafi'i) derived opposite rulings from different authentic narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Chain Disagreement
The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri was narrated by a group (jamā'ah) with a connected chain (mawsool) up to the Prophet, but Ya'qub al-Qari narrated it as mursal from 'Ata'. Determine which version is stronger based on number and reliability of narrators.
The term 'mursal' means the link of the Companion is missing; Hanafis accept mursal under conditions, but Shafi'is generally reject it.
2
Apply the Usul Rule of Tarjih
The majority ruled the connected chain as preponderant (rajih) due to multiple strong narrators and support from scholars like Ibn Abd al-Barr and al-Daraqutni. Understand that in usul, a stronger chain normally takes precedence, but other factors may still lead to different choices.
Tarjih (preference) is applied when two proofs conflict; the stronger in chain or meaning prevails.
3
State the Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Abu Hanifa holds that all sajda al-sahw is after salam. His primary proof is the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba, authenticated by al-Tirmidhi, and the hadith of Abu Hurayra (Dhu al-Yadayn). Note that these hadith have strong chains that Abu Hanifa considered more explicit or practical.
The Hanafi school does not reject the hadith of Abu Sa'id; it simply gives priority to other authentic narrations.
4
Compare with the Majority Position and Proof
The majority (including al-Shafi'i) hold that sajda is before salam. Their proof is the connected hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, which explicitly says 'sajda before salam', and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhayna. Al-Tirmidhi even noted that the 'before salam' hadith is more authentic.
The majority relies on the principle that a clear textual statement (nass) should be followed when the chain is strong.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The practical difference: In Hanafi practice, worshippers perform sajda al-sahw after completing the prayer (after salam). In Shafi'i practice, they perform it before salam, except in specific cases like forgetting to perform sajda altogether. This affects the flow of prayer and how it is taught.
The difference is not a matter of validity; both positions are valid within their respective madhhabs.

Source Text

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
خالفهم جميعاً يعقوب بن عبد الرحمن القاري فرواه عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء مرسلاً. لكن روايته لم تقاوم أمام رواية الجمع إذن فالراجح في رواية هذا الحديث الوصل لكثرة العدد وشدة الحفظ. قال الحافظ ابن عبد البر: و الحديث متصل مسند صحيح، لا يضره تقصير من قصر به في اتصاله؛ لأن الذين وصلوه حفاظ مقبولة زيادتهم. وقال في موضع آخر: قال الأثرم: سألت أحمد بن حنبل عن حديث أبي سعيد في السهو، أتذهب إليه؟ قال: نعم أذهب إليه، قلت: إنهم يختلفون في إسناده، قال: إنما قصر به مالك وقد أسنده عدة منهم: ابن عجلان وعبد العزيز بن أبي سلمة ثم إن هذا الحديث قد تناوله الإمام العراقي الجهبذ أبو الحسن الدارقطني في علله وانتهى إلى ترجيح الرواية المسندة.
أثر هذا الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء (موضع سجود السهو)
اختلف الفقهاء في موضع سجود السهو؛ فذهب أكثر العلماء إلى تصحيح الرواية الموصولة، وأخذوا بالحديث السابق، وقالوا إن السجود كله قبل السلام، وهو قول أكثر الفقهاء، وإليه ذهب الشافعي، وأحمد في رواية. وحديث أبي سعيد نص صريح على أن السجود في الزيادة قبل السلام. واحتجوا لذلك أيضاً بما رواه عبدالله بن بحينة؛ قال: «صلى لنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ركعتين من بعض الصلوات. ثم قام فلم يجلس. فقام الناس معه فلما قضى صلاته، ونظرنا تسليمه كبر فسجد سجدتين، وهو جالس قبل التسليم ثم سلم». وهذا صريح في أن السجود من النقص يكون قبل السلام... وخالف في ذلك بعض الفقهاء، فذهبوا إلى أن سجود السهو كله بعد السلام، روي هذا عن بعض السلف، وإليه ذهب أبو حنيفة. والحجة لهم
1. ما صح عن زياد بن علاقة، قال: «صلى بنا المغيرة بن شعبة؛ فنهض في الركعتين؛ فسبح به من خلفه؛ فأشار إليهم: قوموا فلما فرغ من صلاته، وسلم، ثم سجد سجدتين للسهو؛ فلما انصرف قال رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصنع كما صنعت». وهذا الحديث صححه الإمام الترمذي وقال: «و العمل على هذا عند أهل العلم ثم قال: (ومن رأى قبل التسليم فحديثه أصح 2. ما صح عن أبي هريرة: «أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم انصرف من اثنتين فقال ذو اليدين): أقصرت...
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text. They all were contradicted by Ya'qub ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Qari, who narrated it from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' as mursal. But his narration did not stand against the narration of the group. So the preponderant in the narration of this hadith is the connected version due to the large number and strong memory. Al-Hafiz Ibn Abd al-Barr said: The hadith is connected, attributed, and authentic. The omission of those who omitted its connection does not harm it because those who connected it are reliable memorizers whose addition is acceptable. He said elsewhere: Al-Athram said: I asked Ahmad ibn Hanbal about the hadith of Abu Sa'id concerning forgetfulness: Do you adopt it? He said: Yes, I adopt it. I said: They differ about its chain. He said: Only Malik omitted its connection, and several have connected it: Ibn 'Ajlan and Abd al-Aziz ibn Abi Salama. Then this hadith was examined by the expert Iraqi Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni in his 'Ilal, and he concluded that the connected narration is preponderant.
The effect of this hadith on the disagreement of jurists (the position of sajda al-sahw).
The jurists differed concerning the position of sajda al-sahw. Most scholars accepted the connected narration and took the previous hadith, and said that all prostration is before the salam. This is the view of most jurists, and to it went al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration. The hadith of Abu Sa'id is explicit that prostration for increase is before the salam. They also argued with what was narrated by Abdullah ibn Buhayna: He said: The Messenger of Allah led us in two rak'ahs of one of the prayers. Then he stood up and did not sit. So the people stood with him. When he finished his prayer and we looked for him to say the salam, he said the takbir and prostrated two prostrations while sitting before the salam, then he said the salam. This is explicit that prostration for deficiency is before the salam. But some jurists disagreed and held that all prostration of forgetfulness is after the salam. This is reported from some predecessors, and Abu Hanifa went to it. Their evidence:
1. What is authentic from Ziyad ibn 'Illaqah: He said: Al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba led us in prayer; he stood up after two rak'ahs, so those behind him glorified Allah, and he gestured to them to stand. When he finished his prayer and said the salam, he then prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness. When he left, he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah do as I did. This hadith was authenticated by al-Tirmidhi, and he said: The practice according to this among the people of knowledge. Then he said: 'And whoever holds that it is before the salam, his hadith is more authentic.' 2. What is authentic from Abu Hurayra: 'That the Prophet turned away from two [rak'ahs] and Dhu al-Yadayn said: Has the prayer been shortened? ...'
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage demonstrates how a disagreement in the chain of a hadith leads to a difference in fiqh rulings. The hadith in question is about the prostration of forgetfulness (sajda al-sahw). The author first discusses the chain of the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: some narrated it as mursal (disconnected), but the majority narrated it as musnad (connected) and mawsool. The preponderant view is that the connected version is correct, due to the larger number and reliability of its narrators. This is confirmed by Ibn Abd al-Barr and the analysis of al-Daraqutni. Consequently, most jurists (including al-Shafi'i and Ahmad in one narration) adopt the rule that all sajda al-sahw is performed before the taslim. As proof, they also cite the hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhayna, which clearly shows the Prophet performing sajda before salam. However, Abu Hanifa and some others hold that all sajda al-sahw is after the salam. Their evidence includes the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba, where the Prophet prostrated after salam, and the hadith of Abu Hurayra (partially cited). Al-Tirmidhi authenticated the hadith of al-Mughira and noted that it is acted upon by scholars, while acknowledging that the hadith for before salam is more authentic. This illustrates that even when the chain is strong, jurists may prefer different proofs or interpretations, leading to valid ikhtilaf within the madhhab.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer.
موصول (mawsool): A hadith with a connected chain of narration up to the Prophet.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where a Tabi'i narrates directly from the Prophet, omitting the Companion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the majority of jurists ruled that sajda al-sahw is before salam?
A) They preferred the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba.
B) They considered the connected chain of the hadith of Abu Sa'id to be stronger.
C) They followed the practice of Abu Hanifa.
D) They used qiyas (analogy) with the prostration of recitation.

Key Takeaway
Chain disagreement does not invalidate a hadith; it leads to different tarjih (preference) in usul, resulting in valid fiqh differences between schools.

Timing of Sujud al-Sahw: Analyzing Hadith Evidence for Three Opinions
Analyzing hadith evidence for three juristic opinions on sujud al-sahw timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three juristic opinions on the timing of sujud al-sahw and explain how each opinion derives its ruling from the same hadith evidence using usul principles.

Core Idea
The timing of sujud al-sahw—before or after salam—is a direct consequence of how jurists interpret the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn and Ibn Buhayna.

This passage takes you into the heart of ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement) in Islamic law, showing how the same Prophetic actions can yield different rulings depending on how broadly or narrowly the evidence is applied. You will see three distinct opinions on when to perform sujud al-sahw, each rooted in a careful reading of hadith. Understanding this will sharpen your ability to trace rulings back to their textual sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Hadiths
Locate the two primary hadiths discussed: the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn (increase: speech and walking) and the hadith of Ibn Buhayna (deficiency: leaving the first tashahhud). Note how each hadith describes a different type of error.
These two hadiths are the core evidence for all opinions.
2
Classify Each Hadith by Type of Error
Determine whether the error in each hadith is a deficiency (naqs) or an increase (ziyada). Dhu al-Yadayn involves an increase (speaking), while Ibn Buhayna involves a deficiency (omitting tashahhud).
This classification is crucial for understanding the dispute.
3
Trace the Legal Reasoning (Ta'lil) of Each Opinion
For each opinion, identify the illah (effective cause) they derive from the hadith. The first opinion (Malik/Shafi'i/Ahmad) generalizes from each hadith: deficiency → before salam; increase → after salam. The second opinion (Abu Khaythama etc.) holds that all sujud is before salam except two specific exceptions. The Hanafi opinion (implied) uses the hadith of Thawban and the general practice for after salam.
The difference in generalization scope is what creates the ikhtilaf.
4
Examine the Textual Categories (Fi'l, Amr, etc.)
Classify the Prophetic actions in the hadiths as fi'l (action) or qawl (statement). Determine whether the action is bayan (clarifying) or ta'sis (establishing a new ruling). This affects the weight of the evidence.
This step connects to usul al-fiqh categories.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Difference)
State the practical consequence of each opinion: when exactly does a person perform sujud al-sahw? For example, for an unintentional extra rak'ah, the first opinion says after salam, the second says before salam (unless it falls under an exception).
This shows why the dispute matters for everyday prayer.

وهذا دليل عَلَى أن السجود من الزيادة يَكُون بَعْدَ السلام؛ لأن النبي تكلم. وَفِي رِوَايَة مُسْلِم: «أَلَهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلاة والسلام قام فدخل المنزل»، والمشي والكلام زيادة. ما روي عن ثوبان، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لكل سهو سجدتان بَعْدَ السلام». وهذا الحَدِيث ضعفه البَيْهَقِي). وأجيب بأن إسماعيل إذا حدث عن أهل بلده فروايته عَنْهُمْ صَحِيحَة، وهذا مِنْها ) . إلا أن علة الحَدِيث زُهَيْر بن سالم العنسي) قَالَ عَنْهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِي: حمصي منكر لَمْ يَسْمَع من ثوبان». وذهب بَعْض الفُقَهَاءِ إِلَى: أن السجود إذا كَانَ عن نقص في الصَّلاة فمحله قَبْلَ السلام، وإذا كَان زيادة فمحله بَعْدَ السلام، وَهُوَ مَذْهَب مَالِك وأحد قَوْلي الشَّافِعي وإحدى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ عن الإمام أحمد. والحجة لَهُمْ: حَدِيث عَبْد الله بن بحينة السابق؛ فإنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سجد لتركه التشهد الأول سجدتين قَبْلَ السلام وهذا من نقص في الصَّلاة؛ فحملوا عَلَيْهِ كُلّ نقص، وجعلوا السجود لأجله قَبْلَ السلام. و استدلوا بحديث ذي اليدين؛ فإن النبي له سجد بَعْدَ السلام، لما حصل في الصَّلاة من زيادة الكلام والمشي؛ فحملوا عَلَيْهِ كُلّ زيادة وجعلوا السجود لأجلها بَعْدَ السلام. وذهب بعضهم إلى أن السجود كله قَبْلَ السلام إلا في موضعين، فيكون بَعْدَ السلام وهما: إذا سلم من نقص في صلاته، أو تحرى الإمام فبنى على غالب ظنه. وبذلك قَالَ أبو خيثمة، وسليمان بن دَاوُد، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن الإمام أحمد، واختاره بغض الشافعية، وَهُوَ مَذْهَب الظاهرية. والحجة لَهُمْ: أن السجود إنما شرع لجبر خلل وقع في الصَّلاة؛ فالمعقول أن يَكُون محله قبل السلام، ويستثنى من ذَلِكَ مَا ورد النص بأنه يَكُون بَعْدَ السلام، وَقَدْ ورد ذَلِكَ في النقص، وَهُوَ حَدِيث عبدالله بن بحينة. وفيما إذا تحرى الشاك فبنى عَلَى غالب ظنه ؛ وَذَلِكَ لما صَحَّ عن ابن مَسْعُود لله عن النَّبي : إذا شك أحدكم في صلاته فليتحر الصَّوَاب، وليتم عليه ثُمَّ ليسلم ثُمَّ يسجد سجدتين).
This is evidence that prostration for increase is after the salam because the Prophet spoke. And in a narration of Muslim: 'He (peace be upon him) stood and entered the house', and walking and speaking are an increase. What is narrated from Thawban from the Prophet: 'For every forgetfulness there are two prostrations after the salam.' This hadith was declared weak by al-Bayhaqi. And it was answered that when Isma'il narrates from the people of his town, his narration from them is authentic, and this is from among them. Except that the defect of the hadith is Zuhayr ibn Salim al-'Ansi; al-Daraqutni said about him: 'A Himsi, munkar, he did not hear from Thawban.' And some jurists went to the view that if the prostration is due to a deficiency in the prayer, its place is before the salam; and if due to an increase, its place is after the salam. This is the madhhab of Malik, one of the two sayings of al-Shafi'i, and one of the two narrations from Imam Ahmad. Their evidence is the previous hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Buhayna: the Prophet prostrated for leaving the first tashahhud two prostrations before the salam - this is from deficiency in the prayer; so they applied to it every deficiency and made prostration for it before the salam. And they used the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn as proof: the Prophet prostrated after the salam due to the increase of speech and walking that occurred in the prayer; so they applied to it every increase and made prostration for it after the salam. And some of them went to the view that all prostration is before the salam except in two cases: when one gives salam from a deficiency in his prayer, or when the imam deliberates and builds on his preponderant guess. This was said by Abu Khaythama, Sulayman ibn Dawud, it is a narration from Imam Ahmad, chosen by some Shafi'is, and it is the madhhab of the Zahiris. Their evidence: that prostration was prescribed to repair a defect that occurred in the prayer; rationally its place should be before the salam, except where the text specifies that it is after the salam, and that has been reported in the case of deficiency, namely the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Buhayna. And also in the case where the one in doubt deliberates and builds on his preponderant guess; that is due to what is authentically reported from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet: 'If one of you doubts in his prayer, let him seek what is correct and complete it, then say salam, then prostrate two prostrations.'
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of hadith evidence regarding the timing of sujud al-sahw. It begins by citing the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn, which shows prostrations after the salam due to an increase (speaking). Then it mentions the hadith of Thawban commanding prostrations after the salam for any forgetfulness, but notes its weakness according to al-Bayhaqi and the criticism of Zuhayr ibn Salim. The passage then presents three juristic opinions: (1) The view of Malik, one Shafi'i opinion, and one Ahmad narration: prostrations for deficiency before salam, for increase after salam. Their proof: the hadith of Ibn Buhayna (deficiency: left first tashahhud) and the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn (increase: speech). (2) The view of Abu Khaythama, Sulayman ibn Dawud, another Ahmad narration, some Shafi'is, and the Zahiris: all prostrations before salam except two cases: when one mistakenly gives salam from a deficiency, and when the imam in doubt builds on his preponderant guess. Their proof: prostration is rationally before salam to repair the prayer; exceptions are only where specified by text, i.e., the hadith of Ibn Buhayna and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud about doubt. The passage does not explicitly state the Hanafi position, but elsewhere Hanafis generally hold that sujud al-sahw is wajib and performed after the salam, except in certain cases. This analysis shows how different interpretations of the same hadiths lead to different fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness or error in the prayer.

The timing of sujud al-sahw—before or after salam—depends on how jurists generalize the specific incidents in the hadith, leading to three valid opinions within Sunni fiqh.

Precedence of Marfu' over Mawquf in Authentic Hadith
Analyzing marfu' vs mawquf chains of the hadith on purification from boy's urine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that when a hadith is authentically both marfu' and mawquf, the marfu' version is preferred, and identify the evidence from chain analysis that supports this principle.

Core Idea
When a hadith is both marfu' and mawquf, the marfu' prevails unless evidence shows the raising is mistaken.

This passage analyzes a key hadith on purification from a male child's urine, which is transmitted both as marfu' (raised to the Prophet) and mawquf (stopped at 'Ali). The author examines the chains, citing scholars like al-Bukhari and ad-Daraqutni, to establish a critical usul principle: when both versions are authentic, the marfu' takes precedence. This principle directly impacts how fiqh rulings are derived from such hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its two transmissions
Recognize that the same hadith on purification from a male child's urine is narrated in two forms: marfu' (attributed to the Prophet) and mawquf (attributed to 'Ali ibn Abi Talib).
2
Examine the chain analysis
Follow the author's critique of al-Bazzar's claim that Mu'adh was the only one to narrate it marfu'. Note how the author corrects this by citing 'Abd al-Samad's support and ad-Daraqutni's more precise statement.
Pay attention to how the imams reconciled the two versions.
3
Extract the principle
Understand that when both marfu' and mawquf versions are authentic, the leading hadith scholars give precedence to the marfu' version, unless there are indications that the raising is a mistake.
This is a general usul principle.
4
Apply to fiqh
Recognize that this principle strengthens the Hanafi position (sprinkling suffices for a male child's urine) over the Shafi'i position (washing required), as the marfu' version supports the Hanafi view.
The author mentions this effect without elaborating.

الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن

وصله وإرساله، وقد رجح البخاري صحته وكذا الدارقطني. والرواية المرفوعة رواها معاذ بن هشام، قال: حدثني أبي، عن قتادة، عن أبي حرب بن أبي الأسود، عن أبيه، عن علي بن أبي طالب، مرفوعاً. قال البزار: «هذا الحديث لا نعلمه يروى عن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام إلا من هذا الوجه بهذا الإسناد، وإنما أسنده معاذ بن هشام، عن أبيه، وقد رواه غير معاذ بن هشام، عن قتادة، عن أبي حرب، عن أبيه، عن علي، موقوفاً».

أقول: إطلاق البزار في حكمه على تفرد معاذ بن هشام بالرفع غير صحيح إذ إن معاذاً قد توبع على ذلك تابعه عبد الصمد بن عبد الوارث عند أحمد، والدارقطني، لذا فإن قول الدارقطني كان أدق حين قال: «يرويه قتادة، عن أبي حرب بن أبي الأسود، عن أبيه، رفعه هشام بن أبي عبد الله من رواية ابنه معاذ وعبد الصمد بن عبد الوارث، عن هشام، ووقفه غيرهما عن هشام». والرواية الموقوفة: رواها يحيى بن سعيد، عن سعيد بن أبي عروبة، عن قتادة، عن أبي حرب بن أبي الأسود، عن أبيه، عن علي، فذكره موقوفاً. فالرواية الموقوفة إسنادها صحيح على أن الحديث مرفوع صححه جهابذة المحدثين: البخاري والدارقطني - كما سبق - وابن خزيمة، وابن حبان، والحاكم - ولم يتعقبه الذهبي، ونقل صاحب عون المعبود عن المنذري قال: «قال البخاري: سعيد بن أبي عروبة لا يرفعه وهشام يرفعه وهو حافظ». أقول: هكذا صحح الأئمة رفع هذا الحديث، مع أنه قد صح موقوفاً أيضاً؛ يدل على أن الحديث إذا صح رفعه، ووقفه، فإن الحكم عندهم للرفع، ولا تضر الرواية الموقوفة إلا إذا قامت قرائن تدل على أن الرفع خطأ.

وهذا أثر هذا الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء كيفية التطهر من بول الأطفال و ما دمت قد فصلت القول في حديث علي له مرفوعاً وموقوفاً فسأذكر اختلاف الفقهاء في كيفية التطهر من بول الأطفال.
Chapter Three: Difference in Sanad and Matn. Its connectedness and interruptedness. Al-Bukhari and ad-Daraqutni considered it authentic. The marfu' narration is from Mu'adh ibn Hisham, who said: my father told me, from Qatada, from Abu Harb ibn Abi al-Aswad, from his father, from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, marfu'. Al-Bazzar said: 'We do not know this hadith narrated from the Prophet except from this chain through this route, and only Mu'adh ibn Hisham narrated it marfu' from his father, while others narrated it from Qatada from Abu Harb... mawquf.' I say: al-Bazzar's assertion that Mu'adh was unique in raising it is incorrect because Mu'adh was followed by 'Abd al-Samad ibn 'Abd al-Warith... So ad-Daraqutni's statement was more precise: 'Qatada narrated it from Abu Harb... Hisham raised it in the narration of his son Mu'adh and 'Abd al-Samad, while others stopped it at Hisham.' The mawquf narration is from Yahya ibn Sa'id from Sa'id ibn Abi 'Aruba from Qatada... The mawquf chain is authentic, while the hadith is marfu' as authenticated by leading hadith scholars: al-Bukhari, ad-Daraqutni, Ibn Khuzayma, Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim... The author of 'Awn al-Ma'bud quoted al-Mundhiri that al-Bukhari said: 'Sa'id ibn Abi 'Aruba did not raise it, but Hisham raised it and he is a reliable memorizer.' I say: thus the imams have authenticated the raising of this hadith, even though it is also authentically mawquf. This indicates that when a hadith is authentically both marfu' and mawquf, the ruling according to them is for the marfu' version, and the mawquf narration does not harm except if there are indications that the raising is mistaken. And this is the effect of this hadith on the jurists' difference regarding the method of purification from the urine of male children. Since I have detailed the discussion on the hadith of 'Ali marfu' and mawquf, I will mention the jurists' difference on the method of purification from the urine of male children.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a specific hadith on purification from the urine of a male child, attributed to 'Ali ibn Abi Talib. The author examines the chain of transmission, noting that some narrators transmitted it as marfu' (raised to the Prophet) and others as mawquf (stopped at 'Ali). He critiques al-Bazzar's claim that Mu'adh was unique in raising it, showing that 'Abd al-Samad followed him. He then cites ad-Daraqutni's more precise statement identifying who raised and who stopped it. The author concludes that both the marfu' and mawquf versions are authentic, but the marfu' version is given precedence by the leading hadith scholars (al-Bukhari, ad-Daraqutni, Ibn Khuzayma, etc.). The principle extracted is: when a hadith is authentically both marfu' and mawquf, the ruling is for the marfu', unless there is evidence that the raising is a mistake. This hadith directly impacts the juristic disagreement (ikhtilaf) among fuqaha' regarding the method of purifying from the urine of a male child—whether washing is required or sprinkling suffices. The author promises to detail that difference in the following discussion.

Key Terms
مرفوع (marfu'): A hadith attributed directly to the Prophet Muhammad, as opposed to being stopped at a Companion.
موقوف (mawquf): A hadith attributed to a Companion, not raised to the Prophet.
التطهر من بول الأطفال (al-tatahhur min bawl al-atfal): The ritual purification from the urine of children, specifically male children, a disputed fiqhi ruling.

Key Takeaway
