When Marfu‘ and Mawquf Conflict: The Principle of Preference
Analysis of hadith chains and their impact on fiqh rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that when a hadith is authentic both as marfu‘ and mawquf, the marfu‘ version is given precedence, and evaluate its impact on fiqh rulings regarding purification from infant urine.

Core Idea
When a hadith is both marfu‘ and mawquf, the marfu‘ takes precedence — unless evidence shows the raising is mistaken.

This passage examines the hadith evidence for purification from infant urine, focusing on the hadith of 'Ali which exists in both marfu‘ (raised to the Prophet) and mawquf (stopped at 'Ali) forms. The author demonstrates the usul principle that when both versions are authentic, the marfu‘ is given precedence. This principle directly impacts the ikhtilaf among fuqaha on whether to differentiate between male and female infant urine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transmission forms
In the hadith of 'Ali, note that it is narrated as marfu‘ (attributed to the Prophet) and as mawquf (stopped at 'Ali). Identify the narrators for each chain.
marfu‘ chain: via Hisham; mawquf chain: via Sa'id ibn Abi 'Aruba.
2
Understand the usul principle
The author states that if a hadith is authentic both as marfu‘ and mawquf, the ruling is for the marfu‘ version, unless there are indications of error. This is a key Hanafi usul rule.
Preference for marfu‘ is based on the fact that it directly attributes the statement to the Prophet.

Apply the principle to the hadith of 'Ali

This leads to the Hanafi position of differentiation.

Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi‘i) may interpret the same hadiths differently, leading to different rulings. The author lists additional hadiths that support the sprinkling view.

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن وعبدالصمد بن عبد الوارث، عن هشام، ووقفه غيرهما عن هشام). والرواية الموقوفة: رواها يَحْيَى بن سعيد، عن سعيد بن أبي عروبة، عن قتادة، عن أبي حرب بن أبي الأسود، عن أبيه، عن علي، فذكره موقوفاً(۲). فالرواية الموقوفة إسنادها صَحِيح عَلَى أن الحَدِيث مرفوع صححه جهابذة المُحَدِّثِيْنَ: البُخَارِيّ والدارقطني - كما سبق - وابن خزيمة، وابن حبان)، والحاكم) - وَلَمْ يتعقبه الذهبي ، ونقل صاحب عون المعبود عن المنذري) قَالَ: «قَالَ البُخَارِيّ: سعيد بن أبي عروبة لا يرفعه وهشام يرفعه وَهُوَ حافظ ) . أقول: هكذا صَحْح الأئمة رفع هَذَا الحَدِيث، مَعَ أَنَّهُ قَدْ صَحَ موقوفاً أيضاً؛ يدل عَلَى أن الحَدِيث إذا صَحٌ رفعه، ووقفه، فإن الحكم عندهم للرفع، ولا تضر الرّوَايَة الموقوفة إلا إذا قامت قرائن تدل على أن الرفع خطأ. وهذا أثر هَذَا الحديث في اختلاف الفقهاء كيفية التطهر من بول الأطفال) و ما دمت قد فصلت القَوْل في حَدِيث عَلي له مرفوعاً وموقوفاً فسأذكر اختلاف الفُقَهَاء في كيفية التطهر من بول الأطفال). وقبل أن أذكر آراء الفُقَهَاء أذكر جملة من الأحاديث المتعلقة بالمسألة لأحيل عَلَيْهَا عِنْدَ الإشارة إلى الأدلة طلباً للاختصار. فأقول: ١ صَحَّ عن عائشة زوج النَّبي لا أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: «أتي النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بصبي، فبال عَلَى ثوبه، فدعا النبي الله بماء فأتبعه إياه». رواه مالك (١) ، وزاد أحمد وَمُسْلِم وابن ماجه في روايتهم: وَلَمْ يغسله» (٢). ٢ صح عن أم قيس (۳) بنت محصن «أَنَّهَا أتت بابن صَغِير لَهَا لَمْ يأكل الطعام إلى رَسُول الله ، فأجلسه في حجره، فبال عَلَى ثوبه فدعا رَسُوْلَ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بماء، فنضحه وَلَمْ يغسله». رَواهُ مَالِك، والشيخان: البُخَارِي وَمُسْلِم ) . ٣ حَدِيث عَلِيّ الله وَقَدْ سبق «ينضح من بول الغلام ويغسل من بول الجارية». ٤ صَحَّ عن أبي السمح ) عن النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «يغسل من بول الجارية، ويرش من بول الغلام». بتفصيل أخصر من هَذَا.
Chapter Three / Difference in Chain and Text. And Abd al-Samad ibn Abd al-Warith, from Hisham, and others stopped it from Hisham. The stopped narration: narrated by Yahya ibn Sa'id, from Sa'id ibn Abi 'Aruba, from Qatada, from Abu Harb ibn Abi al-Aswad, from his father, from 'Ali, and mentioned it as stopped. So the stopped narration has an authentic chain, but the hadith is raised and authenticated by the masters of hadith scholars: al-Bukhari and al-Daraqutni - as previously - and Ibn Khuzayma, and Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim - and al-Dhahabi did not comment. The author of 'Awn al-Ma'bud narrated from al-Mundhiri who said: al-Bukhari said: Sa'id ibn Abi 'Aruba does not raise it and Hisham raises it and he is a memorizer. I say: Thus the imams authenticated the raising of this hadith, even though it is also authentic as stopped; indicating that if a hadith is authentic raised and stopped, the ruling with them is for the raised, and the stopped narration does not harm unless there are indications that the raising is mistaken. And this is the impact of this hadith on the difference of the jurists regarding the method of purification from the urine of infants. Since I have already detailed the discussion on the hadith of 'Ali raised and stopped, I will mention the difference of the jurists on the method of purification from the urine of infants. Before I mention the opinions of the jurists, I mention a number of hadiths related to the issue for reference when pointing to evidence seeking brevity. So I say: 1. It is authentic from 'A'isha, wife of the Prophet, that she said: A baby was brought to the Prophet, and he urinated on his garment, so the Prophet called for water and followed it with water. Narrated by Malik, and Ahmad, Muslim, and Ibn Majah added in their narration: and he did not wash it. 2. It is authentic from Umm Qays bint Mihsan that she brought her young son who had not eaten food to the Messenger of Allah, and he sat him in his lap, and he urinated on his garment, so the Messenger of Allah called for water and sprinkled it and did not wash it. Narrated by Malik and the two Shaykhs: al-Bukhari and Muslim. 3. The hadith of 'Ali has preceded: sprinkling from the urine of a male baby and washing from the urine of a female baby. 4. It is authentic from Abu al-Samh from the Prophet that he said: Wash from the urine of a female baby and sprinkle from the urine of a male baby. With more concise detail than this.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of hadith evidence regarding purification from infant urine. The author first discusses the chain of the hadith of 'Ali (muqaddimatan), noting that although it is authentic both as marfu' (raised to the Prophet) and mawquf (stopped at 'Ali), the preferred ruling among hadith scholars is to give precedence to the marfu' version unless there are strong indications of error. This is a key usul principle: when a hadith is both marfu' and mawquf, the marfu' takes precedence. The author then states that this hadith impacts the difference among fuqaha on how to purify from infant urine. Before listing the opinions of the jurists (which are not in this window), he presents four hadiths: (1) 'A'isha's hadith describing that the Prophet followed the urine with water and did not wash it; (2) Umm Qays's hadith that the Prophet sprinkled water and did not wash; (3) 'Ali's hadith differentiating between male and female infants; (4) Abu al-Samh's hadith explicitly stating washing for female and sprinkling for male. These hadiths form the textual basis for the upcoming discussion on ikhtilaf among the schools. The author's approach demonstrates the importance of hadith authenticity and how textual variations (marfu' vs mawquf, wording differences) lead to different fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
الرفع (al-raf‘): Attributing a hadith to the Prophet (marfu‘) as opposed to stopping it at a companion.
الوقف (al-waqf): Attributing a hadith to a companion (mawquf) rather than to the Prophet.
نضح (nadah): Sprinkling water (lightly) without rubbing, considered sufficient for male infant urine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a hadith is authentic both as marfu' and mawquf, what is the default ruling among hadith scholars?
A) The mawquf version is given precedence.
B) The marfu' version is given precedence.
C) Both versions are rejected.
D) The hadith is considered weak.

Key Takeaway
When a hadith is authentic both as marfu‘ and mawquf, the marfu‘ version is given precedence unless there is evidence of error, and this principle directly affects fiqh rulings such as the differentiation between male and female infant urine purification.

Textual Analysis: Washing vs. Sprinkling Infant Urine
Textual evidence and critique of first madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the addition of a phrase in a hadith ('and did not wash it') alters its legal implication and critique the Hanafi interpretation that equates 'following with water' with washing.

Core Idea
The addition 'and did not wash it' transforms 'following with water' from washing to sprinkling.

This lesson examines how a single variation in a hadith text can lead to a major juristic difference. The first madhhab—held by Abu Hanifa and Malik—interprets 'itba' al-ma'' (following with water) as full washing, despite the explicit denial of washing in some narrations. By tracing the textual clues, we uncover the interpretive operation and its critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify key phrases
List the verbs used in each hadith: 'atba'a' (followed), 'nadaha' (sprinkled), 'rasha' (scattered). Note the presence or absence of 'wa lam yaghsilhu' (and did not wash it).
Focus on the hadith of Aisha and Umm Qays.
2
Compare versions
The versions with 'wa lam yaghsilhu' explicitly state the Prophet did not wash the garment. Without it, one might assume washing was intended.
The Malik narration lacks the addition; Ahmad, Muslim, and Ibn Majah include it.
3
Evaluate the Hanafi interpretation
Hanafis claim 'atba'a' and 'nadaha' are figurative for washing, citing other contexts. But here, that interpretation conflicts with the explicit denial.
Al-Tahawi provided evidence that these terms sometimes mean washing, but the critic argues the context here overrides that.
4
Assess the critique
The critic says the explicit 'did not wash' makes the figurative reading impossible; the actions must be mere sprinkling. This shows how textual evidence (ziyada) can resolve ambiguity.
This critique sets the stage for the second madhhab (that sprinkling suffices for a baby boy).

Chapter Three / Difference in Chain and Text. Before I mention the opinions of the jurists, I will mention a number of hadiths related to the issue to refer to them when indicating the evidence, seeking brevity. I say: 1. It is authentically reported from Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, that she said: 'A baby boy was brought to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and he urinated on his garment. So the Prophet called for water and followed it (the urine) with it.' Malik narrated it, and Ahmad, Muslim, and Ibn Majah added in their narration: 'and he did not wash it.' 2. Authentically reported from Umm Qays bint Mihsan that she brought a small son of hers who had not yet eaten food to the Messenger of Allah, and he sat him in his lap. The boy urinated on his garment, so the Messenger of Allah called for water and sprinkled it and did not wash it. Malik and the two Shaykhs, al-Bukhari and Muslim, narrated it. (†) ... 4. Authentically reported from Abu al-Samh from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Wash from the urine of a girl and sprinkle from the urine of a boy.' The jurists differed regarding the rulings derived from these hadiths according to schools, the most famous of which are as follows: The first school: It holds that purification from the urine of an infant – like purification from the urine of an adult – is only by washing it, and there is no difference in that between the urine of an infant who has eaten food or not, just as there is no difference in that between male and female. Abu Hanifa held this, and it is the well-known view of Malik, despite a difference in the manner of washing that suffices for purification from impurity. Abu Hanifa conditions for purification of non-visible impurity multiple washings – three or seven – and wringing after each wash, while Malik did not condition more than pouring water over the impurity so that it immerses it and removes its color, taste, and smell, and he does not require rubbing or wringing for removal of impurity, etc. They interpreted 'following with water,' 'sprinkling,' and 'scattering' – all these terms – as meaning washing. Al-Tahawi extensively cited reports indicating that these terms are sometimes used to mean washing. But this is critiqued: these terms, though sometimes used for washing, in this specific issue do not bear that interpretation because it would lead to a contradiction that the texts are free from.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage introduces the third chapter on the effect of differences in chains and texts on juristic disagreements. The author states that before presenting the jurists' opinions, he will list several hadiths related to the issue for reference. He then provides four hadiths: (1) The hadith of Aisha about a baby urinating on the Prophet's garment, where he 'followed' the urine with water, with an added phrase 'and he did not wash it' in some versions. (2) The hadith of Umm Qays, where the Prophet 'sprinkled' water on the urine and did not wash. (3) [The text has a fragment possibly about Ali, may Allah be pleased with him.] (4) The hadith of Abu al-Samh distinguishing between washing from a girl's urine and sprinkling from a boy's urine. After listing these, the author notes that the jurists differed on the rulings derived. Then he presents the first madhhab: that the urine of an infant, whether it has eaten food or not, and regardless of gender, must be washed like that of an adult. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and the well-known view of Malik. However, they differed on the method: Abu Hanifa requires multiple washings and wringing for non-visible impurities, while Malik only requires pouring water over the impurity until its color, taste, and smell are gone, without needing to rub or wring. Both scholars interpreted the terms in the hadiths ('followed,' 'sprinkled,' 'scattered') as meaning washing, citing al-Tahawi's evidence. The author then critiques this interpretation, arguing that in these specific hadiths, the terms cannot mean washing because that would contradict the clear statement 'and he did not wash it.' This critique sets the stage for the opposing view (likely that sprinkling suffices for a baby boy). The passage demonstrates how differences in interpreting the wording of hadiths (the text) lead to juristic differences.

Key Terms
إتباع الماء (itba' al-ma'): Following the urine with water, i.e., pouring water over it.
نضح (nadah): Sprinkling water, not necessarily washing.
رش (rash): Scattering or sprinkling water.
غسل (ghusl / ghasl): Washing with water, requiring flow and rubbing in Hanafi fiqh.
زيادة (ziyada): Addition to a hadith text, here the phrase 'and did not wash it.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the critique presented in the source, why cannot 'itba' al-ma' in the hadith of Aisha be interpreted as washing?
A) Because the term never means washing in Arabic.
B) Because the hadith has a weak chain.
C) Because the addition 'and he did not wash it' contradicts that interpretation.
D) Because the Prophet only sprinkled the garment of a girl.

Key Takeaway
A single textual variant (ziyada) can reverse the apparent meaning of a hadith and must be accounted for in legal derivation.

Variant Hadith Wordings on Infant Urine: Sprinkling vs Washing
Analyzing how differing hadith wordings lead to three scholarly opinions on infant urine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze variant hadith wordings using Hanafi usul principles (takhsis, bayan) and derive the fiqh ruling on purification from infant urine.

Core Idea
Variant wordings must be coherent; equating 'sprinkling' and 'washing' creates contradiction, proving they are distinct.

This passage examines how different wordings of the same hadith—or closely related hadiths—can lead to divergent fiqh rulings. The author demonstrates that if two terms (sprinkling and washing) were synonymous, the Prophet's actions would be contradictory. Instead, the Hanafi school uses takhsis (specification) and bayan (clarification) to reconcile general evidence on urine impurity with the specific exception for nursing infants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual variants
Read the hadiths of Aisha and Umm Qays. Note the verbs: 'followed it' (أتبعه) and 'sprinkled it' (نضحه). The author argues these cannot mean 'washed' without contradiction.
The conjunction in Abu al-Samh's hadith (عطف النضح على الغسل) further supports distinction.
2
Apply the logical contradiction test
If 'followed' or 'sprinkled' meant 'washed', then the text would say 'he washed it and did not wash it'—a contradiction. This proves the terms are distinct in shari'ah.
This is a common usul technique: if a claim leads to absurdity, the claim is invalid.
3
Dismiss weak attributions
The second madhhab attributing purity or no-wash to al-Shafi'i or Malik is rejected by later authorities (al-Baji, al-Nawawi) as irregular or false. Focus on the third madhhab.
Weak attributions are set aside; only the established position is analyzed.
4
Define the third madhhab's ruling
The third madhhab rules: sprinkling (nadh) suffices for urine of an infant who has not eaten food; after eating, washing is required. Nadh is defined as covering with water without flow.
This definition is crucial: it distinguishes nadh from ghusl by intensity.
5
Respond to Ibn Hazm's objection
Ibn Hazm claimed the hadith of Umm Qays does not specify the condition of not eating. The author replies: general hadiths establish urine impurity and washing, but the specific hadith of Umm Qays provides takhsis (exception). The conjunction of general and specific yields the Hanafi ruling.
This demonstrates the interplay of 'amm (general) and khass (specific) in Hanafi usul.

الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
الشريعة؛ فحديث أم المؤمنين عائشة رضي الله عنها قد جاء بلفظ: «فدعا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بماء فأتبعه ولم يغسله فإذا جعل أتبعه بمعنى غسله فإن المعنى حينئذ يكون فغسله ولم يغسله. وكذلك حديث أم قيس بنت محصن قد جاء بلفظ: «فنضحه ولم يغسله» فلو حمل النضح على معنى الغسل لكان التقدير: فغسله ولم يغسله، وهذا تناقض غير معقول. وأيضاً فإن النبي [؟] مع الطفل الغسل على النصح في حديث علي [؟] وعطف الرش على الغسل في حديث أبي السمح له، والعطف يقتضي المغايرة. فلو أريد بهما معنى واحد، لكان عبثاً يتنزه عنه الشارع. (1)
المذهب الثاني: نسب إلى الشافعي قول: بأن بول الصبي الذي لم يأكل الطعام طاهر. ونسبت رواية إلى الإمام مالك: أنه لا يغسل بول الجارية ولا الغلام قبل أن يأكلا الطعام. لكن ذكر الباجي (2) أن هذه الرواية عن مالك شاذة (3). وذكر النووي أن نقل هذا القول عن الشافعي باطل (4). لذلك لا حاجة للتعليق على هذا المذهب.
المذهب الثالث: ينضح بول الطفل الرضيع الذي لم يأكل الطعام، فإذا أكل الطعام كان حكم بوله كحكم بول الكبير يغسل. وقد فسر هذا المذهب النضح بأنه غمر موضع البول ومكاثرته بالماء مكاثرة لا يبلغ جريانه وتردده وتقطره. فهو بمعنى الغسل الذي سبق ذكره عن مالك (5). وقد اعتمد هذا المذهب حديث أم قيس بنت محصن، فقد جاء بلفظ: «أنها أتت بابن لها صغير لم يأكل الطعام... الخ».
(1) فقه الإمام سعيد بن المسيب 37/1
(2) هو الحافظ أبو الوليد سليمان بن خلف بن سعيد التجيبي الذهبي الباجي ولد سنة (403 هـ) من مصنفاته " المنتقى في الفقه " و" المعاني في شرح الموطأ " و " الاستيفاء"، توفي سنة (474 هـ). وفيات الأعيان 408/2 ، وتذكرة الحفاظ 1178/3 و 1180 ، وشذرات الذهب 344/3.
(3) المنتقى شرح الموطأ 128/1.
(4) شرح صحيح مسلم 583/1-584.
(5) المغني 734/1-735، والحاوي 320/20-321، والتهذيب 206/1.
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
وقد اعترض ابن حزم - القائل: بأن النضح يكفي في التطهير من بول الذكر كبيراً أو صغيراً - بأن تخصيص ذلك بالصبي الذي لم يأكل ليس من كلام النبي، لذلك فالحديث لا دلالة فيه على هذا التحديد (1). ويجاب على ذلك: بأنه نجاسة الأبوال المستتبعة لوجوب غسلها، كل ذلك مستيقن بالأحاديث العامة الدالة على ذلك، كحديث ابن عباس في القبرين اللذين أخبر رسول الله له أن صاحبيهما يعذبان، وقال: «أما أحدهما فكان يمشي بالنميمة، وأما الآخر فكان لا يستنزه من البول». أخرجه البخاري ومسلم (2). وحديث أبي هريرة مرفوعاً: «استنزهوا من البول؛ فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه». رواه أحمد (3)، وابن ماجه (4)، وابن خزيمة (5)، والدارقطني (6)، والحاكم (7)، وصححه البخاري (8). وحديث ابن عباس مرفوعاً: «تنزهوا من البول، فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه». أخرجه البزار (9)، والطبراني (10)، والدارقطني (11)، والحاكم (12). فنجاسة بول الآدمي ووجوب غسله كل ذلك متيقن بهذه الأحاديث، وتخصيص بول الصبي الذي لم يأكل الطعام بالنضح متيقن بحديث أم قيس بنت محصن، وما عدا

Chapter Three / Difference in Sanad and Matn. Sharia; the hadith of Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, came with the wording: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, called for water and followed it (the urine) and did not wash it.' If one makes 'followed it' mean 'washing it', then the meaning would be 'he washed it and did not wash it'. Likewise, the hadith of Umm Qays bint Mihsan came with the wording: 'He sprinkled it and did not wash it.' If one interprets 'sprinkling' as 'washing', then the implied meaning would be 'he washed it and did not wash it', and this is an unreasonable contradiction. Also, the Prophet [?] with the child, washing upon sprinkling in the hadith of Ali [?], and he joined 'sprinkling' with 'washing' in the hadith of Abu al-Samh, and conjunction requires difference. If the same meaning was intended for both, it would be a futile act from which the Lawgiver is free. (1)
Second madhhab: A saying was attributed to al-Shafi'i that the urine of a boy who has not eaten food is pure. A narration was attributed to Imam Malik that he does not wash the urine of a girl or a boy before they eat food. However, al-Baji (2) mentioned that this narration from Malik is irregular (3). And al-Nawawi mentioned that transmitting this saying from al-Shafi'i is false (4). Therefore, there is no need to comment on this madhhab.
Third madhhab: The urine of a nursing infant who has not eaten food is sprinkled. When he eats food, his urine's ruling is like the urine of an adult, it is washed. This madhhab explained 'sprinkling' as covering the place of urine and overwhelming it with water in an overwhelming manner that does not reach flowing, returning, and dripping. So it is like the 'washing' previously mentioned from Malik (5). This madhhab relied on the hadith of Umm Qays bint Mihsan, which came with the wording: 'She brought a small son of hers who had not eaten food... etc.'
(1) Fiqh of Imam Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib 1/37.
(2) He is al-Hafiz Abu al-Walid Sulayman ibn Khalaf ibn Sa'id al-Tujibi al-Dhahabi al-Baji, born 403 AH... (biography omitted).
(3) Al-Muntaqa Sharh al-Muwatta' 1/128.
(4) Sharh Sahih Muslim 1/583-584.
(5) Al-Mughni 1/734-735, al-Hawi 20/320-321, al-Tahdhib 1/206.
Chapter Three / Difference in Sanad and Matn. Ibn Hazm - who says that sprinkling suffices for purification from the urine of a male, whether adult or child - objected that specifying that for the infant who has not eaten food is not from the speech of the Prophet, therefore the hadith has no indication of this specification. The response to that is: The impurity of urines entails the obligation of washing them; all of that is certain from the general hadiths that indicate that, such as the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas about the two graves which the Messenger of Allah informed that their occupants are being punished, and he said: 'As for one of them, he used to walk with slander; and as for the other, he did not avoid urine.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. And the hadith of Abu Hurayra raised: 'Avoid urine, for indeed most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' Reported by Ahmad, Ibn Majah, Ibn Khuzayma, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim, and authenticated by al-Bukhari. And the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas raised: 'Avoid urine, for indeed most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' Narrated by al-Bazzar, al-Tabarani, al-Daraqutni, al-Hakim. So the impurity of human urine and the obligation of washing it are all certain from these hadiths, and the specification of the urine of the infant who has not eaten food with sprinkling is certain by the hadith of Umm Qays bint Mihsan, and beyond that
(1) al-Muhalla 1/101.
(2) Sahih al-Bukhari 1/65 (218) and 2/119 (1361) and 2/124 (1378) and 8/20 (6052), Sahih Muslim 1/166 (292). Also reported by Ahmad, Abd ibn Humayd, al-Darimi, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Ibn Khuzayma. (References continue)
(3) al-Musnad 2/326, 388, 389.
(4) In his Sunan (348).
(5) As mentioned by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in al-Fath 1/336, and it is not in the printed version of Sahih Ibn Khuzayma... (details omitted).
(6) In his Sunan 1/128.
(7) al-Mustadrak 1/183.
(8) al-Tirmidhi transmitted it from him in his 'Ilal al-Kabir: 45 (37).
(9) Kashf al-Astar (243).
(10) In al-Kabir 11 (11104) and (11120).
(11) In his Sunan 1/128.
(12) al-Mustadrak 2/183-184.

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis showing how differing hadith wordings lead to divergent fiqh rulings on infant urine. The author first argues that the verbs 'followed it' and 'sprinkled' in the hadiths of Aisha and Umm Qays cannot be interpreted as 'washing' because that would create a logical contradiction. This reasoning supports a view that distinguishes between sprinkling and washing. The second madhhab (attributed to al-Shafi'i and Malik) is dismissed as unsubstantiated. The third madhhab, which is the relied-upon position, holds that sprinkling suffices for a breastfeeding infant who has not yet eaten solid food, but once the child eats, washing becomes required. Ibn Hazm objects that the hadith of Umm Qays does not explicitly specify the condition of not eating; the author responds by citing general hadiths that establish the impurity of urine and the obligation to wash, and argues that the exception for the infant is proven by the specific hadith of Umm Qays, which is certain in its indication. The passage thus demonstrates how variant wordings (sprinkling vs. washing) and the interplay of general and specific texts yield the Hanafi fiqh ruling.

Key Terms
نضح (nadh): Sprinkling – covering the place of impurity with water without causing it to flow or drip.
غسل (ghusl): Washing – causing water to flow over the impurity, required for adult urine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third madhhab presented in the text, what is the ruling on the urine of a nursing infant who has not yet eaten solid food?
A) It is pure and requires no purification.
B) It must be washed thoroughly like an adult's urine.
C) Sprinkling water over the spot suffices.
D) It is impure but no action is required.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on infant urine purification is derived by specifying general impurity hadiths with the specific hadith of Umm Qays, distinguishing between sprinkling and washing based on the child's diet.

Preferring Mawquf Over Marfu': No Universal Rule in Hanafi Usul
Introduces a model where mawquf narration is preferred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi methodological principle that preference between marfu' and mawquf narrations is determined case-by-case, not by a universal rule.

Core Idea
No universal rule governs marfu' vs mawquf preference; each case stands alone.

This short passage from our text states a key methodological point: the conflict between a marfu' (prophetic) and a mawquf (companion) narration cannot be resolved by a single universal rule. In Hanafi usul, this means the mujtahid must examine each conflict individually, weighing the strength of transmission, context, and other evidence. This principle guards against oversimplification in hadith criticism.

Guided Path
1
Define marfu' and mawquf
Recall that marfu' is a narration attributed directly to the Prophet, while mawquf is attributed to a Companion. Know the basic distinction.
In Hanafi usul, mawquf can sometimes carry the weight of marfu' if the Companion's statement is unlikely to be their own opinion.
2
State the common misconception
Many students assume marfu' always takes precedence over mawquf. Acknowledge this assumption before learning the Hanafi position.
The misconception arises from the general principle that prophetic statements are stronger.
3
State the Hanafi principle from the text
The text explicitly says: 'the ruling on the difference between marfu' and mawquf does not fall under a universal rule.' This means there is no absolute rule that one always outweighs the other.
This is a methodological caution: preference must be determined by additional criteria.
4
Explain why no universal rule exists
Because the strength of a narration depends on its chain, context, and content. A mawquf narration from a prominent Companion with a sound chain may be preferred over a marfu' with a weak chain.
Hanafi usul emphasizes case-by-case assessment (ijtihad).
5
Apply to a hypothetical example
Consider a marfu' hadith saying 'Touching women invalidates wudu' and a mawquf report from Ibn Abbas saying it does not. Which is preferred? According to this principle, we cannot automatically prefer the marfu'; we must examine the chains, the Companion's reliability, and other evidence. In fact, the Hanafi school follows the mawquf position in this case.
This is a real classical example where the Hanafis preferred the mawquf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نموذج آخر وهو مثال لما تترجح فيه الرواية الموقوفة
سبق أن ذكرت أن الحكم في اختلاف الرفع والوقف لا يندرج تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية،
Another model, and it is an example of what the mawquf narration is given precedence over. I have previously mentioned that the ruling on the difference between marfu' and mawquf does not fall under a universal rule.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage introduces a second example (continuing from earlier discussion) showing that in disputes between a marfu' (prophetic) and a mawquf (companion) narration, the preferred narration cannot be determined by a single universal rule. Each case must be examined individually based on the strength of evidence. This is a methodological note in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
المرفوع (al-marfu'): A narration attributed to the Prophet
الموقوف (al-mawquf): A narration attributed to a companion, not the Prophet
قاعدة كلية (qa'ida kulliyya): A universal rule that applies to all cases of its type

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the ruling on preferring marfu' over mawquf?
A) Marfu' is always preferred
B) Mawquf is always preferred
C) It does not fall under a universal rule
D) It depends on the number of narrators

Key Takeaway
No universal rule governs the preference between marfu' and mawquf narrations in Hanafi usul; each conflict must be resolved case-by-case using tarjīḥ criteria.

How Hadith Authentication Shapes Fiqh: Infant Urine Purification
Usul dispute: impact of hadith authentication on fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differed on purification of infant urine, identify the role of hadith authentication (thubut) in that ikhtilaf, and evaluate the later resolution within the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A ruling changes when the Sunnah becomes established — al-Shafi'i's followers revised his position after hadith verification.

This passage illustrates a fundamental principle in Usul al-Fiqh: the authority of a hadith depends on its authenticity (thubut) in the eyes of the mujtahid. Here, the purification of infant urine reveals how Imam al-Shafi'i initially held one view, but once the supporting hadiths were authenticated by his followers, they adopted the distinction between male and female infants. The Hanafi school, having accepted these hadiths from the outset, consistently differentiated between the two.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling and two positions
State the fiqh issue: purification from infant urine. The Hanafi (and majority) position: sprinkling (nadh) suffices for a male infant who hasn't eaten food; washing (ghusl) is required for a female infant. Al-Shafi'i's initial position: sprinkling suffices for both, though he preferred washing for the girl as a precaution.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is the method of purification.
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
The Hanafis rely on hadiths such as those from Ali and Abu as-Samh that explicitly distinguish between male and female infant urine. These are considered established (thabita) by the Hanafi school.
These ahad hadiths are zanni al-thubut but are accepted as reliable.
3
Examine al-Shafi'i's initial position and reasoning
Al-Shafi'i stated that no clear distinction from the established Sunnah was evident to him. He did not reject the hadiths outright but believed they were not proven to his standard of authentication.
His statement shows he was open to accepting them if established.
4
Understand the role of thubut in ikhtilaf
The passage explains that al-Shafi'i's followers later, when the hadiths became established (after compilation and verification by scholars like al-Bayhaqi), unanimously adopted the distinction. This shows that ikhtilaf can stem from differing assessments of transmission strength.
The key usul principle: a mujtahid follows the Sunnah as he knows it.
5
Derive the usul principle
From this case, we learn that the degree of certainty (thubut) of a textual evidence can cause legitimate ikhtilaf. Once the evidence reaches a higher level of authentication, the ruling may be revised even within a school.
This is a cornerstone of Hanafi usul: al-amm yufidu al-wujub only when thubut is firm.

Source Text

الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن
ذَلِكَ مشكوك فِيهِ، فَلاَ يترك اليقين للشك.
والاكتفاء بالنضح في التطهير من بول الرضيع خصه أحمد وجمهور بالصبي الَّذِي لَمْ يأكل الطعام، أما بول الصبية فلا يجزئ فيه إلا الغسل).
٢٥١
الشافعية
أما الشَّافِعِي نَفْسه فَقَدْ نَصَّ عَلَى جواز الرش عَلَى بول الصبي مَا لَمْ يأكل الطعام، واستدل عَلَى ذَلِكَ بالحديث ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وَلاً يبين لي في بول الصبي والجارية فرق من السُّنَّة الثابتة، وَلَوْ غسل بول الجارية كَانَ أحب إلي احتياطاً، وإن رش عَلَيْهِ مَا لَمْ تأكل الطعام أجزأ، إن شاء الله تَعَالَى»(۲).
وَقَدْ ذكر النَّوَوِيِّ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى - أَنَّهُ لَمْ يذكر عن الشَّافِعِي غَيْرِ هَذَا، وَقَالَ البَيْهَقِيّ: والأحاديث المسندة في الفرق بَيْنَ بول الغلام والجارية في هَذَا الباب إذَا ضُمَّ بعضها إلى بَعْض قويت، وكأنها لَمْ تثبت عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيّ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - حِيْنَ قَالَ: ولا يتبين لي في بول الصبي والجارية فرق من السنة الثابتة). وقول الشَّافِعِيّ هَذَا مروي عن النخعي، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن الأوزاعي، ووجه لبعض
الشافعية، ووصفه النَّوَوِيّ : بأنه ضَعِيف ) وهنا يأتي دور حَدِيث علي الله ومثله حَدِيث أبي السمح له خادم النبي ، فهي
أحاديث ثابتة، وَقَدْ فرقت بَيْنَ بول الصبي وبين بول الصبية. وَقَدْ ثبت هَذَا عِنْدَ أحمد؛ لِذلِكَ أخذ بِهِ وفرق بَيْنَهُمَا في الحكم، أما الشَّافِعِي فَقَدْ صرح بأنه لم يثبت عنده من السُّنَّة ما يفرق بَيْنَهُمَا ؛ لِذلِكَ رأى أن النضح يكفي فِيْهِمَا – وإن كَانَ الأحب إليه غسل بول الصبي احتياطاً ؛ وَلَوْ ثبت عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي هَذِهِ الأحاديث لأخذ بها، فهذا هُوَ شأنه وشأن الفُقَهَاء كافة لا يتخطون السنة الثابتة عندهم إلى غيرها، مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا عندهم معارض؛ ولذلك أطبق أصحاب الشَّافِعِي عَلَى الفرق في الحكم بين بول الصبي والصبية لما ثبتت عندهم هذه الأحاديث).
Chapter Three: Variation in Chain and Text. That is doubtful, so certainty is not abandoned for doubt. And the sufficiency of sprinkling in purification from the urine of the infant is specified by Ahmad and the majority to the boy who has not eaten food; as for the girl's urine, only washing suffices. 251. The Shafi'is: As for al-Shafi'i himself, he explicitly permitted sprinkling on the urine of the boy who has not eaten food, and he argued for that with the hadith. Then he said: 'It is not clear to me from the established Sunnah any distinction between the urine of a boy and a girl. If he washes the girl's urine, that is more beloved to me as a precaution, and if he sprinkles on it while she has not eaten food, it suffices, God willing.' An-Nawawi mentioned that nothing else is reported from al-Shafi'i, and al-Bayhaqi said: 'The connected hadiths concerning the distinction between the urine of a boy and a girl in this chapter, when some are joined to others, become strong; it seems they were not established according to al-Shafi'i.' Al-Shafi'i's statement is reported from an-Nakha'i, and it is a narration from al-Awza'i, and a view of some Shafi'is, which an-Nawawi described as weak. Here comes the role of the hadith of Ali and likewise the hadith of Abu as-Samh, the servant of the Prophet; these are established hadiths, and they distinguished between the urine of a boy and that of a girl. And this was established according to Ahmad, so he adopted it and distinguished between them in the ruling. As for al-Shafi'i, he explicitly stated that nothing from the Sunnah that distinguishes between them was established with him; therefore he held that sprinkling suffices for both - although the more beloved to him was washing the boy's urine as a precaution. And if these hadiths had been established with al-Shafi'i, he would have adopted them. This is his way and the way of all jurists: they do not go beyond the established Sunnah to something else, as long as they have no opposing evidence. Therefore, the followers of al-Shafi'i all agreed on the distinction in ruling between the urine of a boy and a girl when these hadiths became established with them.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a dispute analysis demonstrating how varying assessments of hadith authenticity lead to differences in fiqh rulings. The issue is the purification from the urine of an infant: for a male infant who has not yet eaten solid food, sprinkling water (nadh) suffices, while for a female infant, washing (ghusl) is required. The author identifies two positions: the majority (including Imam Ahmad) makes the distinction based on hadiths that differentiate between male and female infants. Al-Shafi'i initially did not find the distinction established in the Sunnah, so he considered sprinkling sufficient for both, though he preferred washing for the girl as a precaution. The passage then notes that later, when the supporting hadiths (such as the hadith of Ali and Abu as-Samh) became established among Shafi'i's followers, they adopted the distinction. This illustrates a key usul principle: jurists follow the established Sunnah as they understand it; when evidence is lacking or unclear, they may differ. The Hanafi madhhab aligns with the majority in distinguishing between male and female infant urine for purification.

Key Terms
النضح (an-nadh): Sprinkling water on the area of urine as a means of purification for a male infant's urine.
الصبي (as-sabi): Male infant who has not yet eaten solid food.
الصبية (as-sabiyyah): Female infant, for whose urine washing is required.
الثبوت (ath-thubut): Establishment or authentication of a hadith as reliable in the view of a scholar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did al-Shafi'i originally not distinguish between male and female infant urine?
A) He considered the hadith evidence insufficiently strong.
B) He rejected the hadith of Ali and Abu as-Samh.
C) He believed all infant urine is pure.
D) He followed the majority opinion.

Key Takeaway
Ikhtilaf in fiqh often stems from differing assessments of hadith authenticity; once evidence becomes established, rulings may be revised within a school.

Preferring the Mawquf Narration: Ablution of Ali
Example of mawquf preference via murajjahat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify preponderating factors (murajjahat) that can cause a mawquf narration to be preferred over a marfu' one, and apply them to a hadith example.

Core Idea
No universal rule: mawquf can trump marfu' when contextual factors align.

In hadith studies, not every marfu' narration automatically outweighs a mawquf one. This lesson explores the nuanced principle of tarjih (preference) through the example of the hadith of Ali's ablution. You will learn how scholars weigh various factors—such as the memorization ability of narrators, the number of chains, and textual consistency—to determine which version of a report is stronger for deriving legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Riwāyāt
Locate the marfu' version (directly from the Prophet through 'A'idh ibn Habib) and the mawquf version (stopped at Ali, as narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba). Note the final part about reciting Quran in janabah.
The marfu' attributes the statement to the Prophet; the mawquf attributes it to Ali.
2
List Applied Murajjahāt
Recall the preponderating factors mentioned: number of narrators, reliability, contextual consistency. The author hints that 'A'idh was opposed, implying other chains preferred the mawquf.
Possible factors: strength of chain, practice of the Companions, absence of contradiction.
3
Evaluate Why Mawquf Was Preferred
Based on the cut-off text, the mawquf was preferred because of the support from other transmissions and possibly because it aligns with the known practice of Ali.
The example shows that a marfu' alone is not decisive.

سبق أن ذكرت أن الحكم في اختلاف الرفع والوقف لا يندرج تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية، فَقَدْ تترجح الرِّوَايَة الموقوفة، وَقَدْ تترجح الرِّوَايَة المرفوعة؛ وَذَلِكَ حسب المرجحات والقرائن المحيطة بالرواية، وهذه المرجحات مختلفة متفاوتة؛ إِذْ قَد تترجح رِوَايَة الأحفظ، أو الأكثر أو الألزم)، وما إلى غَيْر ذَلِكَ من المرجحات التي يراها نقاد الحَدِيث وصيارفته ومما رجحت فِيهِ الرِّوَايَة الموقوفة:
مَا رَواهُ عائذ بن حبيب ، قَالَ: حَدَّثَني عامر بن السمط ، عن أبي الغريف)، قَالَ: أَتي عَلِيٌّ بوَضوء، فمضمض واستنشق ثلاثاً، وغسل وجهه ثلاثاً وغسل يديـه وذراعيه ثلاثاً ثلاثاً، ثُمَّ مسح برأسه، ثُمَّ غسل رجليه، ثُمَّ قَالَ: هكذا رأيت رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم توضأ، ثُمَّ قرأ شَيْئاً من القُرْآن، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «هَذَا لِمَنْ لَيْسَ بجنب، فأما الجنب فَلَا، وَلَا آية."
رواه الإمام أحمد بن حَنْبَل ، والبخاري في " تاريخه "، وَالنَّسَائِي في "مُسْنَد" علي، وأبو يعلى ، والضياء ، جميعهم من طريق عائد بـ هذا الإسناد.
والذي يهمنا من هَذَا الحَدِيث طرفه الأخير. وَقَدْ خولف عائذ في هَذَا الحَدِيث فَقَدْ أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة من طريق
Another example of when the mawquf narration is preferred. We have previously mentioned that the ruling on the difference between marfu' and mawquf does not fall under a universal rule. Sometimes the mawquf narration is preferred, and sometimes the marfu' narration is preferred, depending on the preponderating factors and contextual clues surrounding the narration. These preponderating factors are varied and graded; sometimes the narration of the more memorizer is preferred, or the more numerous, or the more constant, and other such factors considered by hadith critics and experts. Among the cases where the mawquf narration is preferred: what 'A'idh ibn Habib narrated: 'Amir ibn as-Simt told me from Abu al-Gharif, who said: 'Ali was brought water for ablution. He rinsed his mouth and nose three times, washed his face three times, washed his hands and forearms three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet. Then he said: This is how I saw the Messenger of God perform ablution. Then he recited something from the Quran, then said: This is for one who is not in a state of janabah; as for the one in janabah, not even one verse.' Imam Ahmad, al-Bukhari in his Tarikh, an-Nasa'i in his Musnad of 'Ali, Abu Ya'la, and ad-Diya' all narrated it from 'A'idh ibn Habib through this chain. What concerns us from this hadith is its last part. And 'A'idh was opposed in this hadith, for Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it from another chain...
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage provides an example of a methodological rule in usul al-hadith: that when a hadith is transmitted both as marfu' (raised to the Prophet) and mawquf (stopped at a Companion), one cannot apply a blanket rule preferring one over the other. Instead, the preference depends on various preponderating factors (murajjahat) such as the memorization ability of the narrator, the number of narrators, or the consistency of the transmission. The author gives the example of a hadith about 'Ali's ablution, where he demonstrates the Prophet's method and then adds a statement about reciting Quran only when not in janabah. The key issue is whether the final statement ('This is for one who is not in a state of janabah...') is part of the marfu' part or is 'Ali's own comment. In the chain through 'A'idh ibn Habib, it appears as marfu', but Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it as mawquf. The author notes that the mawquf version was preferred in this case (due to factors not fully detailed in the cut-off text). This illustrates that tarjih (preponderance) is based on careful evaluation of all evidentiary clues, not on a simple rule that marfu' always trumps mawquf.

Key Terms
الرواية الموقوفة (al-riwayah al-mawqufah): A narration that is attributed to a Companion and not raised to the Prophet.
الرواية المرفوعة (al-riwayah al-marfu'ah): A narration that is attributed directly to the Prophet.
المرجحات (al-murajjahat): Preponderating factors that cause one narration to be preferred over another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A marfu' narration is always preferred over a mawquf one.
B) Preference between mawquf and marfu' depends on preponderating factors.
C) The narration of 'A'idh ibn Habib is always correct.
D) Reciting Quran in ablution is allowed for all states.

Key Takeaway
No universal rule: mawquf can be preferred over marfu' when preponderating factors (murajjahat) support it, as in the hadith of Ali's ablution.

Deriving the Ruling on Junub Recitation: Hadith Transmission and Usul
Analyzing the effect of hadith transmission differences on a fiqh ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul methodology to evaluate conflicting narrations and derive the ruling on junub reciting the Quran.

Core Idea
The marfu' hadith, though weak in chain, is preferred due to corroborating evidence, leading to prohibition.

This passage examines how differences in hadith transmission (marfu' vs mawquf) affect fiqh rulings. Using the example of a junub reciting the Quran, we see how Hanafi usul principles guide the preference of evidence despite chain weakness. You will learn to trace the derivation from the hadith to the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting narrations
Determine which version is marfu' (attributed to Prophet) and which is mawquf (attributed to 'Ali). Note the transmitters: four narrators vs. 'A'idh ibn Habib.
The marfu' version comes from 'Abdullah ibn Salamah; the mawquf from multiple reliable chains.
2
Evaluate authenticity (thubut) of each version
Use hadith criticism: al-Daraqutni declared the mawquf authentic; al-Tirmidhi declared the marfu' hasan sahih, but many scholars weakened it. Determine the weight of each in Hanafi usul.
Hanafi usul accepts ahad hadith if conditions are met; here tarjih is applied.
3
Apply the principle of tarjih for conflicting evidence
The Hanafi school prefers the marfu' version because it is corroborated by other narrations and the majority of scholars used it as evidence. Tarjih is based on the strength of corroboration (shawahid).
Tarjih is a key usul tool when thubut is contested.
4
Extract the ruling from the operative phrase
In the marfu' hadith: 'he used to teach us the Quran in every state as long as he was not junub.' The explicit exception (istithna') indicates prohibition during janabah.
The operative phrase is 'ma lam yakun junuban'.
5
State the final Hanafi position and note the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafi ruling: junub is prohibited from reciting the Quran, even a single verse. Some scholars (like some Malikis) allow it based on mawquf or analogy, but the majority prohibits.
Thamarah: a junub may not recite, but may read meanings without touching the mushaf according to some.

الفصل الثالث: الاختلاف في السند والمتن
شريك بن عبد الله النخعي. والدارقطني، عن يزيد بن هارون، والبيهقي، عن الحسن بن صالح بن حي. وأخرجه البيهقي أيضاً، عن خالد بن عبد الله؛ أربعتهم: شريك بن عبد الله، ويزيد بن هارون، والحسن بن صالح بن حي، وخالد بن عبد الله، رووه عن عامر بن السمط، عن أبي الغريف الهمداني، عن علي بن أبي طالب، موقوفاً. فرواية الجمع أصح وأولى؛ وقد صحح الإمام الدارقطني الوقف، فقال عقب الرواية الموقوفة: «هو صحيح عن علي». ومما يؤكد صحة رواية الجمع أن عبد الرزاق أخرجه عن سفيان الثوري، عن عامر الشعبي، وابن المنذر أخرجه عن إسحاق، عن عامر السعدي؛ كلاهما (عامر الشعبي وعامر السعدي) عن أبي الغريف، عن علي بن أبي طالب، به موقوفاً. كل هذا يؤكد خطأ عائذ بن حبيب في رفعه الحديث؛ ولعل هذا مما أنكر عليه.

اختلف العلماء في حكم قراءة القرآن للجنب على قولين:

Chapter Three: Difference in Isnad and Matn. Shareek ibn Abdullah al-Nakha'i. And al-Daraqutni, from Yazid ibn Harun, and al-Bayhaqi, from al-Hasan ibn Salih ibn Hayy. And al-Bayhaqi also narrated it from Khalid ibn Abdullah; all four: Shareek ibn Abdullah, Yazid ibn Harun, al-Hasan ibn Salih ibn Hayy, and Khalid ibn Abdullah, narrated it from 'Amir ibn al-Samt, from Abu al-Gharif al-Hamdani, from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, as mawquf. So the collective narration is more authentic and preferable; and Imam al-Daraqutni declared the mawquf narration authentic, saying after the mawquf narration: 'It is authentic from 'Ali.' And what confirms the authenticity of the collective narration is that 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated it from Sufyan al-Thawri, from 'Amir al-Sha'bi, and Ibn al-Mundhir narrated it from Ishaq, from 'Amir al-Sa'di; both (Amir al-Sha'bi and Amir al-Sa'di) from Abu al-Gharif, from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, as mawquf. All of this confirms the error of 'A'idh ibn Habib in raising it (to the Prophet); and perhaps this is among what was criticized against him. Their evidence: They used the previous hadith of 'Ali raised to the Prophet. Ibn al-Mundhir said: 'Those who disliked a junub reciting the Quran used the hadith of 'Ali as evidence.' And it is as if they gave precedence to the marfu' over the mawquf, as is the madhhab of a group of hadith scholars; or because the hadith has corroborating evidences that may strengthen it. 2. What 'Abdullah ibn Salamah narrated from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, used to teach us the Quran in every state as long as he was not junub.' Ibn Abi Shaybah, Imam Ahmad, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Abu Ya'la narrated it with this wording, and others narrated it with similar wording. Al-Tirmidhi said: 'The hadith of 'Ali is hasan sahih.' Thus said Imam al-Tirmidhi - may Allah have mercy on him - except that the great hadith scholars weakened this hadith. Imam al-Nawawi said: 'The majority contradicted al-Tirmidhi and weakened this hadith.' And al-Bukhari said: 'He said.'
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of how differences in hadith transmission (isnad and matn) lead to differences in fiqh rulings. The specific example is the prohibition of a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) from reciting the Quran. The author first analyzes the transmission of a key hadith attributed to 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). Multiple narrators report it as mawquf (a statement of 'Ali), and this is deemed more authentic by al-Daraqutni and others. The marfu' version (attributed to the Prophet) is considered an error by the narrator 'A'idh ibn Habib. Despite this, the majority of jurists (including Hanafis, Malikis, Shafi'is, and Hanbalis) hold that a junub is prohibited from reciting the Quran, using the marfu' version as evidence. They argue that even if the chain is weaker, the marfu' version is supported by other corroborating narrations. The hadith narrated by 'Abdullah ibn Salamah explicitly states that the Prophet taught the Quran in every state except when junub, which is strong evidence for prohibition. Al-Tirmidhi rated it hasan sahih, but many prominent hadith scholars like al-Bukhari and al-Nawawi considered it weak. This illustrates the usul principle that the authenticity of a hadith (thubut) and its indication (dalalah) are critical in deriving rulings. The Hanafi school, like the majority, adopts the prohibition due to the strength of the evidence, even though the hadith's chain is disputed. The passage shows how ikhtilaf in hadith evaluation directly impacts fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, after sexual intercourse or emission of semen.
حديث مرفوع (hadith marfu'): A hadith attributed to the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) in statement or action.
حديث موقوف (hadith mawquf): A hadith attributed to a Companion (Sahabi), not reaching the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is prohibited.
C) It is disliked but not prohibited.
D) It depends on the length of recitation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul allows using a hadith with a disputed chain if it has corroborating evidence and is adopted by the majority of scholars, leading to the prohibition of junub reciting the Quran.

Dispute on Junub Reciting Quran: Hadith Criticism and Evidence
Analyzing the sanad and matn of the prohibition hadith and presenting the permissibility view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critically evaluate the hadith evidence for and against the permissibility of a junub reciting the Quran, and identify the usul principles at play.

Core Idea
A weak hadith cannot establish a prohibition; the sahih hadith of Aisha supports permissibility.

This passage examines a classic usul dispute: may a person in janabah recite the Quran? The ruling hinges on hadith criticism. One side relies on a weak hadith that allegedly prohibits; the other side invokes a sahih hadith that the Prophet remembered Allah in all states, and argues that Quran is dhikr. This lesson walks you through the sanad and matn analysis that determines the strength of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opposing rulings
What does each side rule and on what basis? The first opinion prohibits the junub from reciting Quran; the second permits it.
2
Examine the prohibition hadith's sanad
List the narrator criticisms (Ahmad, Bukhari, etc.) and the effect on authenticity. The narrator Abdullah ibn Salamah changed in old age, and the chain is considered weak.
3
Analyze the matn of the prohibition hadith
Does it contain an explicit prohibition or just describe an action? Even if accepted as hasan, the text does not explicitly forbid; it only describes the Prophet's action.
4
Evaluate the permissibility evidence
What is the hadith of Aisha, and how do proponents use it to argue that Quran is dhikr? The hadith is sahih and general in indicating remembrance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does this dispute make in a Hanafi vs. other school's fatwa? The Hanafi school prohibits, while the permissibility view allows recitation without touching the mushaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث الاختلاف في السند والمتن

شُعْبَة عن عُمَرو بن مرة قَالَ: كَانَ عَبْد الله يحدثنا فنعرف وننكر، وكـانَ قَدْ كبر . وَقَالَ الخَطَّابِيّ: «كَانَ أحمـد يـوهـن هَذَا الحَدِيث». وَقَالَ البزار عقب تخريجه الحَدِيث: (ذ) وهذا الحَدِيث لا نعلمه يروى بهذا اللفظ إلا عن عَلِيّ، وَلا يروى عن عَلِيّ إلا من حَدِيث عَمْرو بن مرة، عن عبد الله بن سلمة، عن عَلِي، وَكَانَ عَمْرو بن مرة يحدّث عن عَبْد الله بن سلمة فَيَقُولُ: يعرف في حديثه وينكر).

وَقَالَ البُخَارِيّ: «عبد الله بن سلمة أبو العالية الكوفي لا يتابع في حديثه»، وَقَالَ الشَّافِعي في سُنَن (حرملة: إن كَانَ هَذَا الحَدِيث ثابتاً، ففيه دلالة عَلَى تحريم القُرْآن عَلَى الجنب»، وَقَالَ في (جماع كِتَاب الطهور): «أهل الحديث لا يثبتونه».

قَالَ البَيْهَقِي: «إنما قَالَ ذَلِكَ لأن عَبْد الله بن سلمة راويه كَانَ قَدْ تغير، وإنما رَوَى هَذَا الحَدِيث بعدما كبر، قَالَه شُعْبَة». ومع كُلّ هَذَا فَقَدْ قَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: «الحق أَنَّهُ من قبيل الحَسَن، يصلح للحجة». وعلى تقدير صلاحيته للاحتجاج، فلا حجة فِيهِ؛ لأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ فِيهِ نهي عن أن يقرأ الجنب القُرْآن، وإنما هُوَ فعلٌ مِنْهُ عَلَيْهِ السلام لا يلزم، وَلاً بين ال أَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يمتنع من قِرَاءة القُرْآن من أجل الجنابة). .. وما روي عن ابن عُمَر عن النَّبي الله قَالَ : لا تقرأ الحائض وَلاَ الجنب شيئاً من القُرْآن ... وَهُوَ حَدِيث ضَعِيف لضعف إسناده فَهُوَ من رِوَايَة إِسْمَاعِيْل بن عياش، عن موسى بن عُقْبَة، عن نافع عن ابن عُمَر. وإسماعيل بن عياش منكر الحديث عن أهل الحجاز وأهل العراق، وحديثه هَذَا عن أهل الحجاز؛ لأن موسى بن عقبة مدني 

القول الثاني: يجوز للجنب قراءة القُرْآن وهذا القَوْل مروي عن ابن عَبَّاس، وسعيد بن المسيب، وعكرمة، وربيعة الرأي، وسعيد بن جبير، وَهُوَ قَوْل ابن حزم الظاهري ونقله عن دَاوُد وعامة أصحابهم واختاره ابن المنذر . والحجة لهذا المذهب:

ما صَحَّ أَنَّهُ عليه الصَّلاة والسلام: «كَانَ يذكر الله عَلَى كُلِّ أحيانه». أخرجه مسلم وغيره.

قالوا: والقُرْآن ذكر.

قَالَ أبو بَكْر بن المنذر: «فَقَالَ بعضهم : الذكر قَدْ يَكُون بقراءةِ القُرْآن وغيره، فكلُّ ما وقع عَلَيْهِ اسم ذكر الله فغير جائز أن يمنع مِنْهُ أحدٌ، إذا كَانَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يمتنع من ذكر الله عَلَى أحيانه».
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text. Shu'bah from 'Amr ibn Murrah said: 'Abdullah used to narrate to us and we would recognize and reject, and he had grown old.' Al-Khattabi said: 'Ahmad used to weaken this hadith.' Al-Bazzar said after citing the hadith: 'This hadith is not known to be narrated with this wording except from 'Ali, and it is not narrated from 'Ali except from the hadith of 'Amr ibn Murrah, from 'Abdullah ibn Salamah, from 'Ali. And 'Amr ibn Murrah would narrate from 'Abdullah ibn Salamah and say: Things are recognized and rejected in his hadith.' Al-Bukhari said: ''Abdullah ibn Salamah Abu al-'Aliyah al-Kufi is not followed in his hadith.' Al-Shafi'i said in Sunan Haramlah: 'If this hadith is established, then it indicates the prohibition of the Quran for the junub.' And he said in Jami' Kitab al-Taharah: 'The people of hadith do not affirm it.' Al-Bayhaqi said: 'He only said that because 'Abdullah ibn Salamah, its narrator, had changed, and he only narrated this hadith after growing old, as Shu'bah said.' Despite all this, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'The truth is that it is of the category of hasan, suitable for proof.' And assuming its suitability for proof, there is no proof in it, because there is no prohibition in it against the junub reciting the Quran; rather, it is an action of his, peace be upon him, which is not binding, and it is not clear that he refrained from reciting the Quran because of janabah. And what is narrated from Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet ﷺ: 'The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite anything of the Quran'... And it is a weak hadith due to the weakness of its chain, as it is from the narration of Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash, from Musa ibn 'Uqbah, from Nafi', from Ibn 'Umar. And Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash is denounced in hadith from the people of Hijaz and the people of Iraq, and this hadith of his is from the people of Hijaz because Musa ibn 'Uqbah is Medinan. The second opinion: It is permissible for the junub to recite the Quran. This opinion is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, 'Ikrimah, Rabi'ah al-Ra'y, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, and it is the opinion of Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri, and he narrated it from Dawud and most of their companions, and Ibn al-Mundhir chose it. The evidence for this madhhab: What is authentically reported that he, peace be upon him, 'used to remember Allah in all of his states.' Narrated by Muslim and others. They said: And the Quran is remembrance. Abu Bakr ibn al-Mundhir said: 'Some said: Remembrance can be by reciting Quran and otherwise, so everything that falls under the name of remembrance of Allah is not permissible to be prevented from anyone, since the Prophet ﷺ did not refrain from remembrance of Allah in his states.'
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents a classical usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the ruling for a person in a state of major ritual impurity (junub) reciting the Quran. The passage is structured in two parts: first, a detailed critique of the chain (sanad) and text (matn) of the hadith that prohibits the junub from reciting; second, the presentation of the opposing view that permits it, with its evidence. The author does not explicitly take a side but provides the arguments. The first part shows that the prohibition is based on a hadith that many scholars, including Ahmad and Bukhari, weakened due to the narrator 'Abdullah ibn Salamah, whose memory deteriorated with age. Even if the hadith is considered hasan by Ibn Hajar, it does not explicitly contain a prohibition; it only describes the Prophet's action, which is not necessarily binding. The second part cites the well-known hadith of Aisha that the Prophet used to remember Allah in all states, and the reasoning that since the Quran is remembrance, it should not be prevented. This dispute illustrates how differences in evaluating the authenticity and indication of hadith lead to different fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
سند (sanad): The chain of narrators transmitting a hadith, which in this passage is critically examined for reliability
متن (matn): The text of the hadith, which in this passage is examined to determine whether it contains an explicit prohibition or merely describes an action

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the prohibition hadith is considered weak according to the passage?
A) It contradicts the Quran
B) The narrator Abdallah ibn Salamah changed in old age
C) The matn is explicit prohibition
D) It is only narrated by one companion

Key Takeaway
The dispute over junub reciting Quran illustrates how hadith criticism (sanad and matn) directly affects fiqh rulings, and how a weak hadith cannot override authentic evidence.

Apparent vs Actual Continuity in Hadith Chains
Not all apparently continuous chains are actually continuous; discontinuity may be discovered by critics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between apparent continuity (ittisal) and actual discontinuity (inqita') in a hadith chain and apply the principle that explicit claims of hearing do not guarantee continuity.

Core Idea
Apparent continuity does not guarantee actual continuity; critical scholars uncover hidden discontinuities.

In hadith criticism, a chain that appears continuous may still be weak due to hidden discontinuity. This lesson explores how scholars detect such flaws and why a simple statement of hearing (sam') is not always reliable.

Guided Path
1
State the rule about continuity
Recall that continuity (ittisal) is an essential condition for hadith authenticity. A munqati' (disconnected) chain is weak.
2
Identify the critical method
Understand that explicit claims of hearing (sam') do not guarantee continuity; critical imams may detect errors or hidden interruptions.
3
Analyze the example
Consider the narration by Ahmad ibn Mani': the chain appears continuous (Kathir → Ja'far → al-Zuhri), but critical scholars may find that Ja'far did not actually hear from al-Zuhri, revealing discontinuity.
The example is cut off; we assume the scholars identified an inqita'.
4
Apply the principle of ziyadat al-thiqa
When one chain appears continuous and another shows discontinuity, the conflict is resolved similarly to the rules for accepting additional trustworthy narrators. Sometimes discontinuity is preferred, sometimes continuity.
See earlier discussion on ziyadat al-thiqa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثالث: تعارض الاتصال والانقطاع تقدم الكلام بأن الاتصال شرط أساسي لصحة الحديث النبوي، وعلى هـذا فالمنقطع ضعيف لفقده شرطاً أساسياً من شروط الصحة، وقد أولى المحدثون عنايتهم في البحث والتنقير في الأحاديث من أجل البحث عن توفر هذا الشرط من عدمه؛ وذلك لما له من أهمية بالغة في التصحيح والتضعيف والتعليل. وتقدم الكلام أن ليس كل ما ورد فيه التصريح بالسماع فهو متصل؛ إذ قد يقع الخطأ في ذلك فيصرح بالسماع في غير ما حديث، ثم يكشف الأئمة النقاد بأن هذا التصريح خطأ، أو أن ما ظاهره متصل منقطع، وهذا ليس لكل أحد إنما هو لأولئك الرجال الذين أفنوا أعمارهم شموعاً أضاءت لنا الطريق من أجل معرفة الصحيح المتصل من معرفة الصحيح المتصل من الضعيف المنقطع. إذن فليس كل ما ظاهره الاتصال متصلاً، فقد يكون السند معللاً بالانقطاع. وعليه فقد يأتي الحديث مرة بسند ظاهره الاتصال، ويُروى بسند آخر ظاهره الانقطاع، فيرجح تارة الانقطاع وأخرى الاتصال، ويجري فيه الخلاف الذي مضى في زيادة الثقة. وأمثلة ذلك كثيرة. منها ما رواه أحمد بن منيع (۳)، قال حدثنا كثير هشام، قال: حدثنا جعفـــر بـــن بـرقان)، عن الزهري
The third type: Conflict between continuity and discontinuity. It was previously stated that continuity is an essential condition for the authenticity of a prophetic hadith, and accordingly the disconnected (munqati') is weak due to lacking an essential condition. The hadith scholars have devoted their attention to investigating and scrutinizing hadiths to examine the fulfillment of this condition, because of its great importance in authentication, weakening, and defect identification. It was also previously stated that not every hadith that includes an explicit claim of hearing (sam') is actually continuous; for error may occur where one explicitly claims hearing in a hadith, then critical imams uncover that this explicit claim is wrong, or that what appears continuous is actually disconnected. This is not for everyone but only for those men who spent their lives as lamps illuminating our path to know the authentic continuous from the weak disconnected. So, not everything that appears continuous is continuous; the chain may be defective with discontinuity. Accordingly, a hadith may come once with a chain that appears continuous, and be narrated with another chain that appears disconnected, then sometimes the discontinuity is preferred, sometimes the continuity, and the disagreement that occurred regarding the addition by a trustworthy narrator applies to it. Examples of this are many. Among them is what Ahmad ibn Mani' narrated: he said: Kathir ibn Hisham narrated to us, he said: Ja'far ibn Burqan narrated to us from al-Zuhri...
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage introduces the third category of disagreement: the conflict between apparent continuity (ittisal) and actual discontinuity (inqita') in hadith chains. It reiterates that continuity is a fundamental condition for hadith authenticity; a munqati' hadith is weak because it fails this condition. Scholars have invested great effort in verifying whether this condition is met, as it critically impacts authentication (tashih), weakening (tadh'if), and defect identification (ta'lil). The text warns that a mere explicit claim of sam' (hearing) in a chain does not guarantee true continuity; critical scholars may detect errors or hidden discontinuities. This expertise is limited to specialized scholars who have devoted their lives to this science. Consequently, a hadith may be transmitted with two different chains—one apparently continuous and one apparently disconnected—and based on further investigation, either the continuity or the discontinuity may be preferred. This situation parallels the earlier discussion on the acceptance of an addition by a trustworthy narrator (ziyadat al-thiqa). The text provides an example: the narration from Ahmad ibn Mani' via Kathir ibn Hisham and Ja'far ibn Burqan from al-Zuhri. This example likely illustrates a case where one chain appears continuous but another reveals discontinuity, though the full example is cut off.

Key Terms
الاتصال (al-ittisal): The condition that every narrator in the chain actually heard the hadith from the preceding narrator, making the chain continuous.
الانقطاع (al-inqita'): The absence of continuity in the chain, where a narrator is missing or did not actually hear from the previous one, rendering the hadith weak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about a hadith that appears to have a continuous chain but may actually be discontinuous?
A) It is always considered authentic until proven otherwise.
B) It may be discovered by critical imams that the explicit claim of hearing is erroneous.
C) Such a hadith is automatically classified as weak.
D) The conflict between continuity and discontinuity never occurs in reliable transmissions.

Key Takeaway
Not every chain that appears continuous is truly continuous; critical examination of narrators is essential to verify actual hearing (sam').

Hadith Criticism: Muttasil vs Mursal and Its Impact on Legal Evidence
Analyzing the chain of a hadith on breaking fast voluntarily.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi usul principles to evaluate conflicting hadith chains and determine the operative ruling from a mursal hadith.

Core Idea
Chain criticism can overturn a hadith's authenticity; Hanafis accept mursal as proof under conditions.

In this lesson, we examine a case study where multiple narrators transmit a hadith through a muttasil (connected) chain, but later investigation reveals the correct version is mursal (disconnected). This analysis is crucial in Hanafi usul because the acceptance of mursal hadith affects the strength of the legal evidence. You will learn how to weigh conflicting chains and understand why Hanafis accept mursal narrations under certain conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing chains
Locate the muttasil chain (al-Zuhri from 'Urwa from 'A'ishah) and the mursal chain (al-Zuhri from 'A'ishah directly, omitting 'Urwa). Note which narrators support each version.
The muttasil version is supported by seven narrators; the mursal by eight.
2
Evaluate the reliability of narrators
Assess the strength of each narrator in the muttasil chain. Some are weak (e.g., Salih ibn Abi al-Akhdar) or have flaws (e.g., tadlis). Contrast with the reliability of those supporting the mursal version (e.g., trusted scholars like Malik).
Tadlis (obfuscation in transmission) can weaken a chain.
3
Apply criteria for preferred chain
Use Hanafi principles: prefer the version transmitted by more trustworthy narrators, and consider external evidence (e.g., al-Zuhri's own statement that he did not hear from 'Urwa). The majority of critics favored the mursal.
Mursal of a Tabi'i is accepted by Hanafis if the narrator is reliable and the hadith is supported.
4
Derive the ruling from the accepted chain
Once the mursal chain is accepted, the hadith's command (اقضيا يوماً آخر مكانه) is taken as evidence. In Hanafi fiqh, this indicates that breaking a voluntary fast obligates making it up (wajib), not fard, because the evidence is zanni.
The ruling is derived only after establishing the chain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث الاختلاف في السند والمتن
... عن عروة)، فأكلنا منه، فجاء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فبدرتني إليه حفصة، وكانت ابنة أبيها، فقالت: يا رسول الله، إنا كنا صائمتين فعرض لنا طعام اشتهيناه فأكلنا منه، قال: «اقضيا يوماً آخر مكانه». أخرجه الترمذي، والبغوي، وأخرجه غيرهما من طريق جعفر.
عائشة قالت كنت أنا وحفصة صائمتين فعرض لنا طعام اشتهيناه
متصلاً.
هكذا روی هذا الحديث جعفر بن برقان عن الزهري عن عروة، عن عائشة،
وقد توبع على روايته، تابعه سبعة من أصحاب الزهري على هذه الرواية وهم:
١. صالح بن أبي الأخضر، وهو ضعيف يعتبر به عند المتابعة. ٢. سفيان بن حسين، وهو ثقة في غير الزهري باتفاق العلماء.
٣. صالح بن كيسان، وهو ثقة.
٤. إسماعيل بن إبراهيم بن عقبة، وهو ثقة.
٥. حجاج بن أرطأة، وهو صدوق كثير الخطأ والتدليس.
٦. عبد الله بن عمر بن عمر العمري، وهو ضعيف.
٧. يحيى بن سعيد الثقة، فهؤلاء منهم عن الزهري عن عروة، عن عائشة، متصلاً، إلا أنه قد تبين بعد التفتيش والتمحيص والنظر أن رواية الاتصال خطأ والصواب: أنّه منقطع بين الزهري وعائشة، وذكر عروة في الإسناد خطأ.
ومنهم من يصلح حديثه للمتابعة قَدْ رووا الحديث أجمعهم،
لذا قال الإمام النسائي عن الرواية الموصولة: هذا خطأ، وقد فسّر المزي مقصد النسائي فقال: يعني أن الصواب حديث الزهري، عن عائشة وحفصة مرسل). وقد نص كذلك الترمذي على أن رواية الاتصال خطأ والصواب أنه منقطع وذكر الدليل القاطع على ذلك، فقال: روي عن ابن جريج، قال: سألت الزهري، قلت له: أَحدَّثَكَ عروة، عن عائشة؟ قال: لم أسمع عن عروة في هذا شيئاً، ولكني سَمِعتُ في خلافة سليمان بن عبد الملك من ناس عن بعض من هذا سأل عائشة عن الحديث.
ومن قبل سأل الترمذي شيخه البخاري فَقَالَ: «سألت محمد بن إسماعيل البخاري عن هذا الحديث، فقال: لا يصح حديث الزهري، عن عروة، عن عائشة. وحكم أبو زرعة وأبو حاتم الرازيان بترجيح الرواية المنقطعة على الموصولة. قلت: قَدْ رواه الثقات الأثبات من أصحاب الزهري منقطعاً، وهم ثمانية أنفس:
١. صالح بن أبي الأخضر، وهو ضعيف يعتبر به عند المتابعة. ٢. سفيان بن حسين، وهو ثقة في غير الزهري باتفاق العلماء.
٣. صالح بن كيسان، وهو ثقة.
٤. إسماعيل بن إبراهيم بن عقبة، وهو ثقة.
٥. حجاج بن أرطأة، وهو صدوق كثير الخطأ والتدليس.
٦. عبد الله بن عمر بن عمر العمري، وهو ضعيف.
٧. يحيى بن سعيد الثقة، فهؤلاء منهم عن الزهري عن عروة، عن عائشة، متصلاً، إلا أنه قد تبين بعد التفتيش والتمحيص والنظر أن رواية الاتصال خطأ والصواب: أنّه منقطع بين الزهري وعائشة، وذكر عروة في الإسناد خطأ.
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text... from 'Urwa: 'We ate from it, then the Messenger of Allah came, and Hafsah hurried to him - she was his daughter - and said: O Messenger of Allah, we were fasting and food we desired was presented to us, so we ate from it.' He said: 'Make up for it with another day.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and al-Baghawi and others via Ja'far. 'A'ishah said: 'I and Hafsah were fasting and food we desired was presented to us, so we ate from it' as a connected chain. Thus this hadith was narrated by Ja'far ibn Burqan from al-Zuhri from 'Urwa from 'A'ishah, and he was followed in his narration by seven of al-Zuhri's students: 1. Salih ibn Abi al-Akhdar (weak, used for corroboration). 2. Sufyan ibn Husayn (trustworthy regarding other than al-Zuhri). 3. Salih ibn Kaysan (trustworthy). 4. Isma'il ibn Ibrahim ibn 'Uqbah (trustworthy). 5. Hajjaj ibn Arta'ah (truthful but makes many errors and tadlis). 6. 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar al-'Umari (weak). 7. Yahya ibn Sa'id (trustworthy). All narrated from al-Zuhri from 'Urwa from 'A'ishah as connected, but after investigation it became clear that the connected narration is mistaken; the correct version is that it is disconnected between al-Zuhri and 'A'ishah, and the mention of 'Urwa in the chain is an error. Some of them are suitable for corroboration. Thus al-Nasa'i said about the connected narration: 'This is an error.' Al-Mizzi explained al-Nasa'i's intention: 'He means that the correct version is the hadith of al-Zuhri from 'A'ishah and Hafsah as mursal.' Al-Tirmidhi also stated that the connected narration is wrong and that it is disconnected, providing decisive proof: he narrated from Ibn Jurayj: 'I asked al-Zuhri: Did 'Urwa narrate from 'A'ishah? He said: I heard nothing from 'Urwa about this, but I heard during the caliphate of Sulayman ibn 'Abd al-Malik from some people that someone asked 'A'ishah about the hadith.' Earlier, al-Tirmidhi asked his teacher al-Bukhari about this hadith, and he said: 'The hadith of al-Zuhri from 'Urwa from 'A'ishah is not authentic.' Abu Zur'ah and Abu Hatim al-Raziyy ruled in favor of the disconnected narration over the connected one. I say: Trustworthy, reliable narrators among al-Zuhri's students narrated it as disconnected, eight in number: [then repeats list].
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a detailed case study in hadith criticism, specifically analyzing the chain (sanad) of a hadith about two women (Aisha and Hafsa) breaking their voluntary fast and the Prophet's ruling that they must make up one day. The author presents two versions: a muttasil (connected) chain via al-Zuhri from Urwa from Aisha, and a mursal (disconnected) chain where Urwa is omitted. The author lists seven narrators who support the muttasil version, but then critiques them, noting that some are weak or have issues like tadlis. After investigation, the preferred view is that the muttasil narration is mistaken; the correct version is mursal. This is supported by statements from major hadith critics like al-Nasa'i, al-Tirmidhi, al-Bukhari, Abu Zur'ah, and Abu Hatim, who all favored the mursal. The passage illustrates how differences in chains (sanad) impact the authenticity of a hadith and consequently the fiqh ruling derived from it. For Hanafi usul, this demonstrates the importance of sanad criticism in determining the strength of a hadith used as legal evidence.

Key Terms
متصل (muttasil): A hadith with a continuous chain of narration from the Companion to the Prophet.
منقطع (munqati'): A hadith with a break in the chain, here specifically mursal (a Tabi'i directly from the Prophet).
الزهري (al-Zuhri): Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, a famous Tabi'i and hadith scholar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Tirmidhi conclude about the hadith of al-Zuhri from 'Urwa from 'A'ishah regarding breaking the fast?
A) It is authentic and should be acted upon.
B) It is a mistake; the correct version is mursal (disconnected).
C) It is fabricated (mawdu').
D) It is acceptable but weak.

Key Takeaway
When evaluating hadith evidence, chain criticism must prioritize narrator reliability over quantity; the Hanafi school accepts mursal hadith from reliable sources as valid proof.

Tarjih Between Conflicting Hadith Chains: The Case of al-Zuhri
Analyzing conflicting chains of a hadith to illustrate tarjih methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principles of tarjih (preponderance) to resolve apparent contradictions between conflicting hadith chains, using the case of al-Zuhri's hadith as a model.

Core Idea
A single authentic chain does not settle it; the weight of multiple chains and direct narrator testimony determines the preponderant version.

In this lesson, we examine a classic case from hadith criticism where scholars faced a contradiction between a connected (muttasil) and a disconnected (munqati') chain for the same hadith. The resolution involves assessing the reliability of narrators, counting the number of chains, and most importantly, considering the direct statement of the main narrator, al-Zuhri, who denied hearing the hadith from 'Urwah. This lesson will equip you with the method of tarjih when dealing with conflicting textual evidence in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Conflicting Chains
Note that the hadith has two versions: one with al-Zuhri from 'Urwah from 'A'ishah (connected), and another with al-Zuhri directly from 'A'ishah (disconnected/mursal).
2
Assess the Narrators in Each Chain
List narrators. The connected chain includes Hajjaj ibn Arta'ah (truthful but frequent mistakes and tadlis). The disconnected chain is supported by eight highly reliable narrators (Malik, Ma'mar, etc.).
3
Consider External Evidence (Qara'in)
Examine al-Zuhri's own statement that he did not hear from 'Urwah, and the opinions of major hadith critics (al-Nasa'i, al-Tirmidhi, al-Bukhari, Abu Zur'ah, Abu Hatim) who declared the connected version an error.
4
Apply Tarjih
Since the disconnected version has more reliable narrators and direct testimony from al-Zuhri, it is preponderant. The connected version is rejected as mistaken.
5
Extract the Usul Principle
This case illustrates that in case of ta'arud (contradiction), tarjih is based on multiple factors: number of narrators, trustworthiness, and corroborating evidence. Hanafi usul applies similar principles when weighing conflicting proofs.

١. مالك بن أنس (١) وهو ثقة إمام أشهر من أن يعرف.
٢. معمر بن راشد (٣)، وهو ثقة ثبت فاضل.
٣. عبيد الله بن عمر العمري (4)، وهو ثقة ثبت.
